Defining Faqir and Miskin: The Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute and the Dropping of Mu'allafatu Qulubuhum
Inter-madhhab dispute over definitions of faqir and miskin, and historical elimination of mu'allafatu qulubuhum.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between faqir and miskin according to the Hanafi school, state the Hanafi position on which is worse off, and explain the consensus that mu'allafatu qulubuhum is no longer a valid zakat category.

Core Idea
Zakat is for eight categories, but mu'allafatu qulubuhum is dropped; the rest are seven, with miskin being worse than faqir in Hanafi fiqh.

This lesson examines the key terminology in zakat distribution. The Quran mentions eight categories of recipients, but one category—those whose hearts are to be reconciled—was dropped by consensus after the Prophet. We focus on the definitions of faqir and miskin and the famous Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute over which is more deserving.

Guided Path
1
Identify the eight categories and which is dropped
Read the chapter title and note that eight categories are listed but mu'allafatu qulubuhum has been dropped by consensus, leaving seven.
The historical narrative about Umar and the caliphate confirms this consensus.
2
Define faqir and miskin in Hanafi school
The faqir is one with minimal property who does not ask; the miskin is one who asks because he has nothing.
Note that Abu Yusuf considers them one category, but the majority Hanafi position distinguishes them.
3
Identify the Hanafi position on severity
Hanafi: miskin is worse off than faqir.
This is based on Quran 90:16 and 58:4.
4
Identify the Shafi'i position and its proof
Shafi'i: faqir is worse off, based on Quran 18:79.
The interpretation of 'miskin' in that verse is that they have some property.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, Hanafis give priority to miskin, Shafi'is to faqir.
The Hanafi position is preferred by the majority of Salaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب المصرف أي في بيان أحكامه، هو بكسر الراء أي مصرف رف الزكاة والعشر، وهم ثمانية مذكورة في الآية: إِنَّمَا الصَّدَقَاتُ لِلْفُقَرَاء (التوبة: ٦٠)، وقد سقط منهم المؤلفة قلوبهم فبقيت سبعة. (ع) هو الفقير أي أحد المصارف السبعة الفقير وهو من له أدنى شيء، وقيل: هو الذي لا يسأل؛ لأنه يجد قدر ما يكفيه للحال. (مسكين) الأصل فيه قوله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّمَا الصَّدَقَاتُ لِلْفُقَرَاءِ وَالْمَسَاكِينِ﴾ (التوبة: ٦٠)، وقد سقط منها المؤلفة قلوبهم؛ وكانوا أصنافا ثلاثة: صنف كان عليها يتألفهم ويعطيهم ليسلموا، وصنف يعطيهم لدفع شرهم، وصنف أسلموا وفي إسلامهم ضعف فيزيدهم بالعطاء تقريرا على الإسلام كل ذلك كان جهادا منه لإعلاء كلمة الله ؛ لأن الجهاد تارة باللسان وتارة بالبيان وتارة بالإحسان ثم في أيام أبي بكر جاء عيينة والأقرع يطلبان أرضاً فكتب لهما بها فجاء عمر الله ومزق الكتاب وقال: إن الله تعالى أعز الإسلام وأغنى عنكم فإن ثبتم عليه وإلا فبينا وبينكم السيف فانصرفا لأبي بكر وقالا : أنت الخليفة أم هو؟ فقال: "هو إن شاء" ولم ينكر عليه ما فعل فانعقد الإجماع على عدم الدفع إليهم. (فتح) والمسكين: أي والثاني المسكين الذي يسأل؛ لأنه لا يجد شيئاً. (مسكين) وهو أسوء حالاً إلخ: وعند الشافعي: الفقير أسوء حالا المسكين؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿أَمَّا السَّفِينَةُ فَكَانَتْ لِمَسَاكِينَ يَعْمَلُونَ فِي الْبَحْرِ﴾ (الكهف: ٧٩)، ولنا قوله تعالى: ﴿أَوْ مِسْكِيناً ذَا مَتْرَبَةٍ ﴾ (البلد : ١٦) معناه التصق بطنه بالتراب من الجوع، وكذا قوله تعالى: فَإِطْعَامُ سِتِّينَ مِسْكِيناً (المجادلة: ٤) خصهم بصرف الكفارة إليهم. (فتح) من الفقير وهو قول عامة السلف وعند الشافعي على عكس ذلك، وعن أبي يوسف: أنهما صنف واحد.
Chapter of the Disbursement: Explanation of its rulings. The chapter title 'al-Masrif' with a kasra on the ra, meaning the place of disbursement of zakat and 'ushr. They are eight categories mentioned in the verse: 'Indeed the charities are for the poor...' (9:60). The 'those whose hearts are to be reconciled' have been dropped from them, leaving seven. (A) 'Al-Faqir' means one of the seven categories, the poor person who possesses minimal property. It is said: he is the one who does not ask, because he finds enough for his immediate needs. (Miskin) The basis for this is His statement: 'Indeed the charities are for the poor and the needy' (9:60). The 'those whose hearts are to be reconciled' were dropped from it; they were three types: a type whom the Prophet would seek to reconcile by giving them to become Muslim, a type he would give to repel their harm, and a type who had converted but their Islam was weak, so he would increase them by giving to strengthen them in Islam. All of that was his striving to elevate the word of Allah; because jihad is sometimes by tongue, sometimes by pen, and sometimes by benevolence. Then in the days of Abu Bakr, 'Uyaynah and Aqra' came requesting land, so he wrote for them. Then Umar came, tore the document, and said: 'Allah has strengthened Islam and made you independent. If you remain firm, then fine; otherwise, there is the sword between us and you.' They went to Abu Bakr and said: 'Are you the caliph or is he?' He said: 'He is, if Allah wills.' And he did not disapprove of what Umar did, so consensus formed on not giving to them. (Fath) 'Al-Miskin': meaning the second category, the needy person who asks, because he possesses nothing. (Miskin) And he is in a worse condition etc.: According to al-Shafi'i, the faqir is in a worse condition than the miskin, due to His statement: 'As for the ship, it belonged to miskin working in the sea' (18:79). Our proof is His statement: 'Or a miskin having dust' (90:16), meaning his stomach clings to the ground from hunger. Likewise His statement: 'Then feeding of sixty miskin' (58:4), specifying them for the expiation. (Fath) from the faqir; and this is the statement of the majority of the Salaf. According to al-Shafi'i, it is the opposite. From Abu Yusuf: they are one category.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the definitions of faqir and miskin and their relative severity, along with historical context on the elimination of the 'mu'allafatu qulubuhum' category. The commentary opens by explaining that the chapter discusses the eight categories of zakat recipients mentioned in Quran 9:60, but that the 'mu'allafatu qulubuhum' (those whose hearts are to be reconciled) have been dropped by consensus after the practice of the Caliphs Abu Bakr and Umar, leaving seven. The first category is 'al-faqir', defined as someone who possesses minimal property and does not beg because he has enough for immediate needs. The second is 'al-miskin', defined as someone who begs because he has nothing. The Hanafi position is that the miskin is worse off than the faqir, citing Quran 90:16 and 58:4. Imam al-Shafi'i holds the opposite view, based on Quran 18:79. The text also notes that Abu Yusuf considers them one category. The historical narrative about Umar and the request of 'Uyaynah and Aqra' explains the consensus on excluding mu'allafatu qulubuhum.

Key Terms
الفقير (al-faqir): One who possesses minimal property and does not ask because he finds enough for immediate needs.
المسكين (al-miskin): One who asks because he possesses nothing.
المؤلفة قلوبهم (al-mu'allafatu qulubuhum): Those whose hearts are to be reconciled; a category of zakat recipients that was dropped after the Prophet's time by consensus.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, who is in a worse condition: the faqir or the miskin?
A) The faqir
B) The miskin
C) Both are equal
D) Neither is defined

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school, following the general Salaf, holds that the miskin is more deserving of zakat than the faqir, and that the category of mu'allafatu qulubuhum is no longer applicable.

The Zakat Collector: Compensation vs Ownership
Ruling on the zakat collector with proof and inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on paying the zakat collector and explain why he may be wealthy and the payment limit of half.

Core Idea
The 'amil is compensated for his work, not given ownership of zakat; thus he can be rich and paid up to half.

The zakat collector ('amil) is one of the eight categories of zakat recipients, but the Hanafi school views his payment as compensation for his service, not as a zakat share. This distinction has practical consequences: even a wealthy collector can be paid, and his payment is capped at half of what he collects. This lesson examines the proof and the inter-madhhab dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is the ruling on paying the 'amil? The text says he can be paid even if rich, but not exceeding half. Identify the hukm level: mubah (permissible) with conditions.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the Quranic verse 'Indeed the charities are for the poor...' The Hanafi school interprets the lam (ل) as indicating consequence, not ownership.
The opposing schools interpret the lam as for ownership, making the 'amil an owner of a share.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The operative word is the lam. The Hanafi argue that the lam is for 'li-bayan al-'aqibah' (consequence), so the 'amil is not an owner but a worker deserving wages.
This is a key usul al-fiqh point.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali hold that the 'amil is one of the eight owners and deserves an eighth of the zakat proceeds.
Their proof is the same verse but they read the lam as for ownership.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is relied upon in the school, as supported by Fath al-Qadir and 'Ayni.
The practical difference: Hanafi limit payment to half, others give an eighth.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(ع) والعامل: أي الثالث العامل ولو غنيا إلا هاشميا، وهو من نصبه الإمام لاستيفاء الصدقات ساعيا كان أو عاشرا، فيعطيه الإمام ما يكفيه وأعوانه، لكن لا يزاد على نصف ما يقبضه (ط) أي عامل الصدقة يعطى له بقدر عمله ذهاباً وإياباً، وكان المال حتى لو حمل أرباب الأموال الزكاة إلى الإمام، أو هلك بما جمعه من المال لا يستحق شيئاً من بيت المال، وأجزأت الزكاة عن المؤدين؛ لأنه بمنزلة الإمام في القبض أو نائب عن الفقير في القبض، فإذا تم القبض سقطت الزكاة وكذا حقه؛ لأنه عمالته في معنى الأجرة، ويتعلق بالمحل الذي عمل فيه فإن هلك سقطت، فيعطيه الإمام وإن كان غنياً؛ لأن ما يأخذه ليس زكاة، وإنما هو بمقابلة عمله، ولكن لا يزاد أداؤه على النصف، وعند الشافعي ومالك وأحمد: يعطى له ثمن الحاصل؛ لأن العامل ثامن ثمانية ذكرت في النص، واللام في ﴿إِنَّمَا الصَّدَقَاتُ لِلْفُقَرَاء للتمليك، وعندنا: اللام فيه لبيان العاقبة أنهم مصارف لا لبيان الاستحقاق. (فتح، عيني) والمكاتب أي الرابع المكاتب ولو لغني لا هاشمي، فيعان المكاتب على أداء بدل الكتابة بصرف الصدقة إليه. (ط) وهو معنى قوله تعالى: ﴿وَفِي الرِّقَابِ ﴾ (البقرة : ۱۷۷) عند أكثر أهل العلم، وأطلقه فعم مكاتب الغني أيضاً، وذكر أبو الليث: لا تدفع إلى مكاتب غني، والصحيح هو الأول، وأما عدم جواز الدفع إلى مكاتب الهاشمي، فظاهر كلامهم الاتفاق عليه وكذا لا فرق بين مكاتب الصغير والكبير.
(A) 'And the worker': meaning the third category, the worker even if rich except a Hashimi. He is the one appointed by the Imam to collect the charities, whether a sa'i or an 'ashir. The Imam gives him sufficient for himself and his assistants, but not exceeding half of what he collects. (T) Meaning the zakat worker is given according to his work going and coming, and the money, even if the owners bring the zakat to the Imam, or if the money he collected perishes, he does not deserve anything from the treasury. And the zakat is valid for the payers, because he is in the position of the Imam in receiving or a deputy for the poor in receiving. So when receipt is completed, the zakat falls, and likewise his right; because his work is like wages, and it is connected to the place where he worked; if it perishes, it falls. So the Imam gives him even if he is rich, because what he takes is not zakat, but rather it is in exchange for his work. But his payment is not increased beyond half. According to al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad: he is given an eighth of the proceeds, because the worker is the eighth of the eight mentioned in the text, and the lam in 'for the poor' indicates ownership. According to us, the lam therein indicates the consequence that they are recipients, not for entitlement. (Fath, 'Ayni) 'And the mukatab': meaning the fourth, the mukatab even if rich, but not a Hashimi. The mukatab is assisted in paying off his kitabah by giving charity to him. (T) And this is the meaning of His statement 'and in the necks' (2:177) according to most scholars. He made it general, so it includes even a rich mukatab. Abu al-Layth mentioned: do not give to a rich mukatab. The correct is the first. As for the impermissibility of giving to a Hashimi mukatab, it is apparent that they agree on it. Likewise, there is no difference between a young and an adult mukatab.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage covers two categories of zakat recipients: the 'amil (zakat collector) and the makatib (slave under contract of emancipation). The 'amil is appointed by the Imam to collect zakat; he may be given a payment for his work even if he is personally rich, but not exceeding half of what he collects. The Hanafi school argues that the payment is compensation (like wages), not zakat ownership, so wealth is not a barrier. The Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali schools view the 'amil as one of the eight recipients and thus entitled to a share (one-eighth) as ownership. The Hanafi position relies on the lam in the verse indicating consequence rather than ownership. The makatib is assisted with zakat to pay off his kitabah, even if he is rich (except a Hashimi). The text notes disagreement: Abu al-Layth says a rich mukatab should not be given, but the correct view is that he may be given.

Key Terms
العامل (al-'amil): The zakat collector appointed by the Imam; given compensation for work.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the maximum an 'amil can be paid from the zakat collected?
A) One-eighth of the total
B) Half of what he collects
C) As much as needed without limit
D) Nothing if he is rich

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school treats the 'amil's payment as compensation for work, not as a zakat share, allowing payment even if rich, up to half of the collected amount.

The Mukatab: Zakat for the Slave Seeking Freedom
Ruling on giving zakat to the mukatab slave with proof and a minor intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on giving zakat to a mukatab and explain the exception for Hashimi.

Core Idea
A mukatab can be given zakat even if he is rich, except a Hashimi; the goal is to help him pay his kitabah.

One of the eight categories of zakat recipients is 'those in bondage' (fi al-riqab). The Hanafi school specifies that this category applies primarily to the mukatab, a slave who has contracted emancipation. This lesson clarifies that wealth of the mukatab is not a barrier, except if he is from the Banu Hashim.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on the mukatab
The text states that the mukatab is the fourth category of zakat recipients. He can be given zakat to help pay off his kitabah even if he is rich, except if he is a Hashimi.
The source cites that Abu al-Layth had a different view, but the correct view is that even a rich mukatab can receive.
2
Locate the dalil
The Quranic verse 'And in the necks' (wa fi al-riqab) is interpreted by most scholars to include the mukatab.
The verse is general.
3
Note the exception for Hashimi
There is consensus that a Hashimi mukatab cannot receive zakat, just as other Hashimi cannot receive zakat.
This is because zakat is not permissible for the family of the Prophet.
4
Note the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf
Abu al-Layth held that a rich mukatab should not be given, but the text says the correct view is the first, which permits it.
This is a minor difference within the Hanafi school.

Zakat — Almsgiving

Debtor, Stranded Warrior, and Wayfarer in Zakat
Defining three zakat categories and their conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for each of the three zakat categories (debtor, stranded warrior, wayfarer) and identify which interpretation of 'fi sabil Allah' is preferred in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Zakat can be given to a debtor who lacks a nisab, a warrior stranded by poverty, or a wayfarer whose wealth is at home.

In addition to the well-known eight categories in Surah al-Tawbah, the Hanafi school further specifies conditions for each. This lesson unpacks three specific categories: the debtor (gharim), the stranded warrior (munqati' al-ghuzat), and the wayfarer (ibn al-sabil). Understanding these conditions prevents misapplication of zakat funds.

Guided Path
1
Identify the category
For each of the three terms (al-madyun, munqati' al-ghuzat, ibn al-sabil), note the Arabic term and its legal definition from the text.
The text defines each in relation to the Quranic verse 9:60.
2
Examine the condition
What makes a person eligible for zakat under that category? For the debtor, he must not have a surplus nisab beyond his debt. For the stranded warrior, he is unable to join the army due to poverty. For the wayfarer, he has wealth at home but not with him.
3
Note the interpretation
For 'fi sabil Allah', there is a difference between Abu Yusuf (stranded warrior) and Muhammad (stranded pilgrim). The passage states Abu Yusuf's view is the more apparent (azhar).
Al-Bada'i extends it to all acts of obedience.
4
Consider the extension
The commentator mentions that 'fi sabil Allah' can include other stranded travelers like hajj pilgrims, and even students of knowledge. The addition of 'munqati' al-ghuzat' is for clarification.
5
Synthesize
Summarize how these three categories fit into the overall scheme of the eight recipients. Know that the debtor and wayfarer are separate categories, while 'fi sabil Allah' is broad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمديون: أي الخامس المديون إذا لم يملك نصابا فاضلا عن دينه. (ط) تفسير للغارم، ويجوز أن يراد بالغارم دين على الناس لا يقدر على أخذه، وليس عنده نصاب فاضل، ولا يكون هاشميا. (فتح) ومنقطع الغزاة: أي السادس منقطع الغزاة بسبب الفقر وهو المراد بقوله تعالى: ﴿وَفِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ ﴾ (التوبة: ٦٠) (ع) أي الذي عجز عن اللحوق بجيش الإسلام، وهذا عند أبي يوسف وهو الأظهر، ومنقطع الحاج عند محمد، وقيل: طلبة العلم، وفسره في "البدائع" بجميع القرب أي فسر المراد في قوله تعالى: ﴿وَفِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ ﴾ (التوبة: ٦٠) فإضافة المنقطع إلى الغزاة للتوضيح؛ ليشمل منقطع الحاج ومنقطع غير الغزاة، وقوله: "ابن السبيل" هو المسافر، وإضافته مجازية لأدنى ملابسة (فتح) وابن السبيل أي السابع المسافر وهو من له مال في وطنه لا معه. (ط) فيدفع أي المزكي الزكاة يعني هو مخير إن شاء يدفع إلى الكل إلخ. (ع) أو إلى صنف : وهو قول عمر بن الخطاب الله وعلي بن أبي طالب الله و ابن عباس لما ومعاذ بن حبل الله وحذيفة ابن اليمان له وجماعة أخرى، ولم يرد عن غيرهم من الصحابة خلاف ذلك، فكان إجماعاً، وقال الشافعي: لا يجوز ما لم يصرف إلى الأصناف السبعة من كل صنف ثلاثة؛ لأن الله تعالى أضاف جميع الصدقات إليهم بلام التمليك، وأشرك بينهم بواو التشريك، وذكرهم بلفظ الجمع وأقله ثلاثة، ولنا قوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِنْ تُخْفُوهَا وَتُؤْتُوهَا الْفُقَرَاءَ فَهُوَ خَيْرٌ لكُمْ (البقرة: ۲۷۱) بعد قوله تعالى: ﴿ إِنْ تُبْدُوا الصَّدَقَاتِ فَنِعِمَّا هِيَ ﴾ (البقرة: ۲۷۱) فعلم أن الفقراء مصارف الصدقات من غير أصناف سبعة واللام للعاقبة أي عاقبة الصدقات للفقراء لا أنها ملكهم؛ إذ لو كانت للتمليك لما جاز له أن يطأ جارية له للتجارة لمشاركة الفقراء فيها؛ ولأن بعض المصارف ليس فيه لام وهو قوله: "وفي سبيل الله" فلا يصح دعوى التمليك، وليس الكل بلفظ الجمع كابن السبيل. (فتح، عيني)
'And the debtor': meaning the fifth, the debtor if he does not possess a nisab beyond his debt. (T) Explanation of 'al-gharim'. It is permissible that 'al-gharim' means a debt on people that he cannot collect, and he does not have a surplus nisab, and he is not a Hashimi. (Fath) 'And the one cut off from war': meaning the sixth, the one cut off from war due to poverty, and that is what is meant by His statement 'and in the path of Allah' (9:60). (A) i.e., the one who is unable to join the army of Islam. This is according to Abu Yusuf and it is the more apparent. According to Muhammad, it is the one cut off from hajj. It is said: it is the seeker of knowledge. It is interpreted in al-Bada'i as all acts of obedience. So the addition of 'cut off from war' is for clarification to include the one cut off from hajj and other than war. His saying 'ibn al-sabil': it is the traveler, and the addition is metaphorical for minimal connection. (Fath) 'And ibn al-sabil': meaning the seventh, the traveler who has wealth in his hometown but not with him. (T) So the zakat payer pays the zakat, meaning he is free to choose: if he wishes he pays to all categories (A) or to one category. This is the saying of Umar ibn al-Khattab, Ali ibn Abi Talib, Ibn Abbas, Mu'adh ibn Jabal, Hudhayfah ibn al-Yaman, and another group. No contrary opinion from other Companions is narrated, so it is consensus. Al-Shafi'i said: it is not permissible unless it is distributed to all seven categories, three of each category, because Allah added all charities to them with the lam of ownership, and made them partners with the waw of partnership, and mentioned them in plural which minimum is three. Our proof is His statement: 'And if you conceal it and give it to the poor, it is better for you' (2:271) after His statement: 'If you disclose the charities, well and good' (2:271). So it is known that the poor are recipients of charities irrespective of the seven categories. And the lam is for consequence, i.e., the consequence of charities is for the poor, not that they own them. For if it indicated ownership, it would not be permissible for him to have intercourse with his slave girl whom he bought for trade because the poor would share in her. Also because some categories do not have the lam, like His statement 'and in the path of Allah', so the claim of ownership cannot be sustained. Not all are in the plural form, like ibn al-sabil. (Fath, 'Ayni)
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage covers three more categories: the debtor (madyun/gharim), the stranded warrior (munqati' al-ghuzat), and the wayfarer (ibn al-sabil). The debtor is defined as someone whose debts exceed his nisab; he may be given zakat to pay off his debts. There is a distinction: Abu Yusuf interprets 'fi sabil Allah' as the stranded warrior; Muhammad as the stranded pilgrim; others include students. The commentary prefers Abu Yusuf's view. Ibn al-sabil is the traveler who has wealth at home but not with him. The major dispute in this passage is about distribution: must zakat be given to all seven categories or can it be given to one? The Hanafi position is that the payer may choose to give to one category or all, based on the actions of many Companions and the verse 2:271 which singles out the poor. Al-Shafi'i requires distribution to all seven, each with at least three recipients, based on the plural and the lam of ownership. The Hanafi response relies on the lam indicating consequence not ownership, and the fact that some categories (like 'fi sabil Allah') have no lam, and some are not in plural.

Key Terms
المديون / الغارم (al-madyun / al-gharim): A debtor who does not have a surplus nisab after deducting debts; can be given zakat.
منقطع الغزاة (munqati' al-ghuzat): One who is stranded from joining the Muslim army due to poverty; interpreted by Abu Yusuf as the meaning of 'fi sabil Allah'.
ابن السبيل (ibn al-sabil): A traveler who has wealth at home but not with him.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the condition for a debtor to receive zakat?
A) He must be bankrupt.
B) He does not have a surplus nisab beyond his debt.
C) He must be a Hashimi.
D) He must be a trader.

Key Takeaway
Debtors, stranded warriors, and wayfarers are eligible for zakat under specific conditions; the preferred Hanafi view includes all stranded travelers in 'fi sabil Allah'.

Zakat Distribution: One Category or All?
Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute on mandatory distribution vs. permissibility of single category.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on giving zakat to a single category, support it with dalil, and contrast it with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Hanafis allow giving all zakat to one category; Shafi'is require distributing to all seven with at least three each.

The Quran lists eight categories of zakat recipients, but does it mandate distribution to all? The Hanafi school, relying on Companion consensus and a verse singling out the poor, holds complete flexibility. Imam al-Shafi'i argues for mandatory distribution. This lesson dissects the proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
The thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafis allow giving zakat to one category; Shafi'is require distribution to all seven categories with at least three in each.
2
State the Hanafi position and dalil
Hanafis rely on Quran 2:271 which says 'give it to the poor' (singular category), and the consensus of Companions (Umar, Ali, Ibn Abbas, etc.).
The text also argues that the lam in 9:60 is for consequence, not ownership.
3
State the Shafi'i position and dalil
Shafi'is rely on Quran 9:60 which uses lam of ownership and waw of partnership, and plural forms which indicate at least three from each category.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Hanafis rebut: 1) If lam indicated ownership, one could not have intercourse with a slave girl because the poor would have a share. 2) Some categories lack lam (e.g., 'fi sabil Allah'). 3) Not all terms are plural (e.g., 'ibn al-sabil' singular).
The response shows the lam indicates consequence (aqibah), not ownership.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi due to Companion consensus and clear textual support. The payer may choose.

Source Text

Paying Zakat to a Dhimmi: Permissibility and Proofs
Ruling on zakat to a dhimmi and its proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on giving zakat to a dhimmi, identify the key evidence (hadith of Mu'adh), and explain the counterarguments of Zufar and al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
Zakat is exclusively for Muslims; the hadith of Mu'adh specifies the recipient community.

This passage examines a key intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab dispute: may zakat be given to a non-Muslim dhimmi? The Hanafi school (majority) says no, based on the Prophet's instruction to Mu'adh. But a Hanafi dissenter, Zufar, and al-Shafi'i engage with the same Quranic verses differently. Understanding this dispute sharpens our feel for how prophetic specification works in fiqh and the role of analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position and primary proof
State the ruling (haram) and the hadith of Mu'adh: 'Take it from their rich and return it to their poor.' This indicates zakat is for the Muslim community.
The hadith is a solitary (ahad) report, but accepted due to consensus on its meaning.
2
Examine Zufar's objection
Zufar argues that Quran 9:60 and 60:8 do not condition Islam for zakat recipients. He holds that Islam is not a requirement.
Zufar is a Hanafi scholar, so this is an intra-madhhab difference.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to Zufar
The Hanafis respond that the hadith of Mu'adh specifies the general command. Additionally, consensus excludes warring non-Muslims (harbi) by analogy; relatives are also excluded. Thus, specification by khabar al-wahid and qiyas is valid.
The text states: 'جاز تخصيصه بخبر الواحد والقياس' (it is permissible to specify it by solitary hadith and analogy).
4
Compare Shafi'i's position and response
Al-Shafi'i also prohibits giving zakat to a dhimmi, but he argues from the same hadith that dhimmi is like a warring person. The Hanafi response distinguishes: verse 60:9 excludes only warring, not dhimmi; the hadith itself is specific to Muslims.
Shafi'i and Hanafi agree on the outcome (prohibition) but differ in reasoning.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
Practical consequence: Hanafi majority prohibit; Zufar permits; Shafi'i prohibits. The relied-upon position is prohibition (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad).
Zufar's view is considered weak (marjuh) in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا إلى ذمي أي لا تدفع الزكاة إلى ذمي عندنا وإن كان فقيراً، وقال زفر الإسلام ليس بشرط؛ لقوله تعالى: لا يَنْهَاكُمُ اللَّهُ عَنِ الَّذِينَ لَمْ يُقَاتِلُوكُمْ فِي الدِّينِ وَلَمْ يُخْرِجُوكُمْ مِنْ دِيَارِكُمْ أَنْ تَبَرُّوهُمْ﴾ (الممتحنة:٨) وقوله تعالى: وإِنَّمَا الصَّدَقَاتُ لِلْفُقَرَاءِ (التوبة:٦٠) من غير قيد بالإسلام، ولنا: حديث معاذ الله "خذها من أغنياءهم وردها إلى فقراءهم"، فإن قيل: لا تجوز الزيادة بخبر الواحد؛ لأنه نسخ؟ قلنا: النص مخصوص بقوله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّمَا يَنْهَاكُمُ اللهُ عَنِ الَّذِينَ قَاتَلُوكُمْ فِي الدِّينِ (الممتحنة: ٩) وأجمعوا على أن فقراء أهل الحرب خرجوا من عموم الفقراء، وكذا أصول المزكي وفروعه وزوجته فجاز تخصيصه بخبر الواحد والقياس، وصح غير الزكاة كصدقة الفطر والمنذور إلى الذمي، وقال الشافعي: لا يجوز؛ لحديث معاذ الله المذكور، فصار كالحربي، ولنا قوله تعالى: ولا يَنْهَاكُمُ الله ولو لا حديث معاذ الله لقلنا بجواز صرف الزكاة للذمي، والحربي خارج بالنص، وعند أبي يوسف: لا يعطى للذمي زكاة، ولا صدقة الفطر، ولا طعام الكفارات والمستأمن كالحربي لا يجوز دفع صدقة ما إليه. (فتح)
'Not to a dhimmi': meaning we do not pay zakat to a dhimmi even if he is poor. Zufar said: Islam is not a condition due to His statement: 'Allah does not forbid you from those who do not fight you in religion and do not drive you from your homes to be righteous toward them' (60:8) and His statement: 'Indeed the charities are for the poor' (9:60) without the condition of Islam. Our proof is the hadith of Mu'adh: 'Take it from their rich and return it to their poor.' If it is said: 'Increase is not permissible by a solitary hadith because it would be abrogation,' we respond: The text is specified by His statement: 'Allah only forbids you from those who fight you in religion' (60:9). And they have consensus that the poor of the warring people are excluded from the general meaning of the poor. Likewise, the principals of the payer (parents), his children, and his wife are excluded. So it is permissible to specify it by a solitary hadith and analogy. Other than zakat, like sadaqat al-fitr and vowed charity is valid to the dhimmi. Al-Shafi'i said: it is not permissible due to the aforementioned hadith of Mu'adh, so the dhimmi becomes like the warring person. Our proof is: Allah's statement (60:8). Were it not for the hadith of Mu'adh, we would say zakat distribution to the dhimmi is permissible. The warring person is excluded by the text. According to Abu Yusuf: neither zakat nor sadaqat al-fitr nor expiation food is given to the dhimmi. The musta'man is like the warring person; it is not permissible to give any charity to him. (Fath)
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute on whether zakat can be given to a dhimmi (a non-Muslim protected citizen of the Islamic state). The Hanafi position (according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, with Zufar differing) is that zakat cannot be given to a dhimmi. The primary evidence is the hadith of Mu'adh: 'Take it from their rich and return it to their poor,' implying that zakat is for Muslims. Zufar argues that the Quranic verses (60:8 and 9:60) do not restrict by Islam, so zakat is permissible. The Hanafi response is that the hadith of Mu'adh specifies the general command, and analogy from the exclusion of warring non-Muslims and relatives supports this. Shafi'i also says it is not permissible, but for a different reason: he equates dhimmi with warring people. The Hanafi response notes that were it not for the hadith, it would be permissible. Abu Yusuf adds that sadaqat al-fitr and expiation food are also not given to dhimmi. The passage shows the nuanced reasoning: zakat is specifically for Muslim community, based on prophetic instruction.

Key Terms
الذمي (al-dhimmi): A non-Muslim living under Islamic protection who pays jizya.
المستأمن (al-musta'man): A non-Muslim given safe passage (aman); treated like a warring person in this ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi view, can zakat be given to a dhimmi?
A) Yes, if he is poor
B) No, it is prohibited
C) Only if he is a relative
D) Only zakat al-fitr, not zakat

Key Takeaway
Zakat is for the Muslim community; giving it to a dhimmi does not fulfill the obligation.

Zakat Disbursement: Categories and the One-or-All Debate
Defines three categories and debates paying zakat to one or all

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on paying zakat to a single category, explain the proofs from Quran and ijma, and contrast it with the Shafi'i requirement.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school permits giving all zakat to one deserving individual — a choice, not a forced distribution.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq defines three specific zakat recipients — the debtor, the stranded fighter, and the wayfarer — and then enters a classic inter-madhhab dispute: can you give all your zakat to just one of the eight categories, or must you spread it across all? The Hanafi school, relying on Qur'anic evidence and Companion consensus, holds that giving to one is perfectly valid. This lesson unpacks the definitions and the proofs behind the dispute.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: the payer may give zakat to all categories or to a single category. This is the established Hanafi view.
The text says 'yadfaʻu ilā kullihim aw ilā ṣinf'.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize Imam al-Shafi'i's position: zakat must be given to all eight categories, with at least three individuals from each.
Shafi'i bases this on his reading of Quran 9:60.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Analyze the Shafi'i dalil: the lam in the verse indicates ownership (lām al-tamlīk), the wāw indicates sharing, and plural requires three.
The verse: 'innamā al-ṣadaqātu lil-fuqarā'i...'
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Examine the Hanafi rebuttal: the lam is for consequence (lām al-ʻāqibah), not ownership; Surah al-Baqarah 2:271 mentions only the poor; some categories lack the lam; and there is ijma of Companions.
The text cites Umar, Ali, Ibn Abbas, etc.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
State the practical difference: Hanafis may concentrate all zakat on one needy person; Shafi'is must split it among multiple categories.
This affects distribution in communities with diverse recipients.

أي أو يدفع واحد منهم
وذكر أبو الليث: لا تدفع إلى مكاتب غني، والصحيح هو الأول، وأما عدم جواز الدفع إلى مكاتب الهاشمي، فظاهر كلامهم الاتفاق عليه وكذا لا فرق بين مكاتب الصغير والكبير. والمديون: [ أي الخامس المديون إذا لم يملك نصابا فاضلا عن دينه. (ط)] تفسير للغارم، ويجوز أن يراد بالغارم دين على الناس لا يقدر على أخذه، وليس عنده نصاب فاضل، ولا يكون هاشميا. (فتح) ومنقطع الغزاة: [ أي السادس منقطع الغزاة بسبب الفقر وهو المراد بقوله تعالى: ﴿وَفِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ ﴾ (التوبة: ٦٠) (ع)] أي الذي عجز عن اللحوق بجيش الإسلام، وهذا عند أبي يوسف وهو الأظهر، ومنقطع الحاج عند محمد، وقيل: طلبة العلم، وفسره في "البدائع" بجميع القرب أي فسر المراد في قوله تعالى: ﴿وَفِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ ﴾ (التوبة: ٦٠) فإضافة المنقطع إلى الغزاة للتوضيح؛ ليشمل منقطع الحاج ومنقطع غير الغزاة، وقوله: "ابن السبيل" هو المسافر، وإضافته مجازية لأدنى ملابسة (فتح) وابن السبيل أي السابع المسافر وهو من له مال في وطنه لا معه. (ط) فيدفع أي المزكي الزكاة يعني هو مخير إن شاء يدفع إلى الكل إلخ. (ع) أو إلى صنف : وهو قول عمر بن الخطاب الله وعلي بن أبي طالب الله و ابن عباس لما ومعاذ بن حبل الله وحذيفة ابن اليمان له وجماعة أخرى، ولم يرد عن غيرهم من الصحابة خلاف ذلك، فكان إجماعاً، وقال الشافعي: لا يجوز ما لم يصرف إلى الأصناف السبعة من كل صنف ثلاثة؛ لأن الله تعالى أضاف جميع الصدقات إليهم بلام التمليك، وأشرك بينهم بواو التشريك، وذكرهم بلفظ الجمع وأقله ثلاثة، ولنا قوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِنْ تُخْفُوهَا وَتُؤْتُوهَا الْفُقَرَاءَ فَهُوَ خَيْرٌ لكُمْ (البقرة: ۲۷۱) بعد قوله تعالى: ﴿ إِنْ تُبْدُوا الصَّدَقَاتِ فَنِعِمَّا هِيَ ﴾ (البقرة: ۲۷۱) فعلم أن الفقراء مصارف الصدقات من غير أصناف سبعة واللام للعاقبة أي عاقبة الصدقات للفقراء لا أنها ملكهم؛ إذ لو كانت للتمليك لما جاز له أن يطأ جارية له للتجارة لمشاركة الفقراء فيها؛ ولأن بعض المصارف ليس فيه لام وهو قوله: "وفي سبيل الله" فلا يصح دعوى
Chapter on Disbursement. And the debtor, and the one cut off from the army, and the wayfarer: so he gives to all of them or to one category, not to a dhimmi. He [the commentator] said: or he gives to one of them. Abu al-Layth mentioned: it is not given to a wealthy mukatib, and the correct is the first. And regarding the non-permissibility of giving to a Hashimi mukatib, their statements show agreement. Similarly, there is no difference between a minor and an adult mukatib. The debtor: that is the fifth [category], the debtor who does not possess a nisab beyond his debt. It is an interpretation of al-gharim. It is also permissible to intend by al-gharim one who has a debt owed to him by people and he cannot collect it, and he does not have a surplus nisab, and he is not Hashimi. The one cut off from the army: that is the sixth, the one cut off from the army due to poverty, and that is what is meant by His statement: 'and in the way of Allah'. That is, the one unable to join the army of Islam. This is according to Abu Yusuf, and it is the most apparent. And the one cut off from pilgrimage according to Muhammad. And it is said: students of knowledge. And in al-Bada'i it is interpreted as all acts of worship. So the addition of 'cut off from the army' is for clarification, to include the one cut off from pilgrimage and other than the army. His statement: 'ibn al-sabil' is the traveler, and its addition is metaphorical due to the slightest connection. And ibn al-sabil: that is the seventh, the traveler who has wealth in his homeland but not with him. So he gives: i.e., the zakat payer gives the zakat, meaning he is given a choice: if he wishes, he gives to all, etc., or to one category. And this is the statement of Umar ibn al-Khattab, Ali ibn Abi Talib, Ibn Abbas, Mu'adh ibn Jabal, Hudhayfah ibn al-Yaman, and a group of others. No opposition from other Companions is reported, so it became consensus. Al-Shafi'i said: It is not permissible unless given to all seven categories, three from each category, because Allah added all sadaqat to them with the lam of ownership, and associated between them with the waw of sharing, and mentioned them in the plural, and the minimum of plural is three. Our evidence is the verse: 'If you conceal them and give them to the poor, it is better for you' after His statement: 'If you disclose the sadaqat, it is good.' So it is known that the poor are the recipients of sadaqat without being limited to seven categories. And the lam is for consequence, i.e., the consequence of sadaqat is for the poor, not that they own it; for were it for ownership, he would not be allowed to have intercourse with his slave-girl used for trade due to the poor sharing in her. And because some recipients do not have a lam in the verse, such as His statement: 'and in the way of Allah.' So the claim is not valid.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage begins the chapter on the disbursement of zakat (bāb al-maṣrif). It first defines three specific categories among the eight: the debtor (al-madyūn), the one cut off from the army (munqaṭiʿ al-ghuzāh), and the wayfarer (ibn al-sabīl). The text clarifies that the debtor is a type of gharim (one in debt), and that it includes both those who owe money and those owed money but unable to collect. For 'munqaṭiʿ al-ghuzāh', there is an intra-Hanafi difference: Abu Yusuf interprets it literally as one unable to join the military expedition, while Muhammad extends it to include one cut off from pilgrimage and others. The preferred view in the text is Abu Yusuf's. The wayfarer is defined as a traveler who has wealth at home but not with him. 

The core legal ruling addressed is the permissibility of paying zakat to a single category (صنف) rather than distributing to all eight. The Hanafi position, attributed to several Companions and deemed consensus (ijmāʿ), is that the payer may give to all categories or to only one. Al-Shafiʿī disagrees, arguing that the Quranic verse (9:60) uses the lam of ownership (lām al-tamlīk) and the waw of sharing (wāw al-tashrīk), and mentions categories in the plural, requiring at least three individuals from each category. The Hanafi response : First, the verse in Surah al-Baqarah (2:271) mentions only the poor, showing that the categories are not exhaustively required. Second, the lam in the verse (9:60) is for consequence (lām al-ʿāqibah), not ownership; otherwise, a merchant could not have intercourse with his trade slave-girl due to the poor's theoretical share. Third, some categories like 'fī sabīlillāh' lack the lam, breaking the pattern. Thus the opponent's claim (daʿwā) is invalid. The relied-upon position (muftā bihī) is the Hanafi view allowing payment to one category.

Key Terms
المديون (al-madyūn): A person in debt who does not own a nisab beyond his debt; a type of gharim.
منقطع الغزاة (munqaṭiʿ al-ghuzāh): A person who is unable to join the army due to poverty; interpreted broadly to include those cut off from other good deeds.
ابن السبيل (ibn al-sabīl): A traveler who has no wealth with him, even if he has wealth in his homeland.
صنف (ṣinf): One of the eight categories of zakat recipients (asnaf).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, is it permissible to give all one's zakat to a single recipient from one category?
A) Yes, the payer may give to one category or to all.
B) No, one must give to at least three from each of the eight categories.
C) Yes, but only to the poor category.
D) No, zakat must be distributed equally among all eight categories.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school allows giving zakat to a single category; this is based on Quranic evidence, Companion consensus, and a nuanced reading of the lam in the zakat verse.

Zakat Cannot Be Used for Non-Tamlik Expenditures
Prohibition of using zakat for mosque building, etc.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school prohibits using zakat for building mosques and other non-tamlik expenditures, and respond to the counter-argument regarding the lam in the Quranic verse.

Core Idea
Zakat must be given as ownership (tamlik); spending on public works lacks tamlik and is invalid.

This passage addresses a crucial ruling in zakat: it cannot be used for building mosques, bridges, or any public works. The Hanafi school derives this from the Quranic verse (9:60), interpreting the lam as indicating ownership. The passage also addresses an objection from other schools and provides a refined response. By the end, you will understand the precise legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Extract the explicit prohibitions: building mosques, shrouding the dead, paying debts, buying slaves to free, and all similar expenditures. Note that these share the characteristic of lacking tamlik.
The list in the text is illustrative, not exhaustive.
2
Understand the condition of tamlik
Tamlik means transfer of ownership to the recipient. For zakat to be valid, the poor must become owners of the funds. Any expenditure that does not result in ownership is invalid.
This is a distinct Hanafi position.
3
Examine the Quranic proof and the lam dispute
The verse 'innama al-sadaqatu li al-fuqara'...' uses the lam, which Hanafis interpret as indicating ownership. Others argue the lam indicates benefit (consequence). The Hanafi response is that even if it is for consequence, eventual ownership is implied, but distribution must occur before that.
Focus on the linguistic argument and its legal impact.
4
Evaluate the cross-madhhab difference
Imam Malik permits spending zakat on public works like mosques because he interprets the lam as benefiting, not ownership. Compare the two positions and note the practical implications.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصح غيرها، وبناء مسجد وتكفين ميت وقضاء دينه وشراء قن يعتق، وأصله الزكاة أي لا تصرف إلى خلافا لمالك وإن علا، وفرعه وإن سفل وزوجته وزوجها وعبده ومكاتبه ومدبّره وأم ولده أي لا يدفع المزكي إلى عبده أي المطلق والمقيد وصح: أي صح دفع غير الزكاة كصدقة الفطر إلى الذمي. (ع) وبناء مسجد : [بالجر عطف على قوله: "ذمي" أي لا تصرف الزكاة إلى بناء مسجد وقنطرة وسقاية وإصلاح طرق ونحوها؛ لعدم التمليك. (ع)] وكذا بناء القناطر وكري الأنهار والحج والجهاد وكل ما لا تمليك فيه فإن قيل: اللام في الآية للعاقبة وجعلتم عدم جواز الزكاة في بناء مسجد وغيره؛ لعدم التمليك؟ قلنا كونها للعاقبة لا ينافي اشتراط التمليك؛ لأنها تدل على ثبوت الملك لهم بعد الصرف إليهم، أما قبله فلا ؛ لعدم تعينهم فجعلها للعاقبة بالنظر إلى ما قبل الصرف لهم. (فتح)
And giving other than zakat (like sadaqat al-fitr) to a dhimmi is valid. And building a mosque, shrouding a dead person, paying his debt, and buying a slave to set free, and his origin (parents) and his branch (children) and his wife and her husband and his slave and his mukatab and his mudabbir and his umm walad: the zakat is not to be given to them. (Commentary clarification: The phrase 'and building a mosque' is grammatically attached to the word 'dhimmi' [in the earlier phrase] i.e., zakat is not to be given for building a mosque, a bridge, a watering station, repairing roads and the like, because there is no ownership. Similarly, building bridges, digging rivers, Hajj, Jihad, and everything in which there is no ownership. If it is said: The lam in the verse (Surah al-Tawbah 9:60) is for consequence, and you have made the impermissibility of zakat in building a mosque etc. due to lack of ownership? We say: Its being for consequence does not negate the requirement of ownership; because it indicates the establishment of ownership for them after paying to them, but before payment, there is no ownership because of their non-specification. So it is made for consequence with regard to before paying to them.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It first states that non-zakat sadaqah (like fitrah) may be given to a non-Muslim (dhimmi). Then it lists categories that cannot receive zakat: building mosques, bridges, etc. The reason given is 'lack of tamlik' (transfer of ownership). Zakat must be given as ownership to the recipient, not spent on public works. An objection is raised that the letter lam in 'li-al-fuqara' (for the poor) indicates consequence, not ownership. The Hanafi response is that even if it indicates consequence, it implies eventual ownership after distribution, but that does not negate the condition of ownership at the time of giving. The ruling is consistent with Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
تمليك (tamlik): Transfer of ownership of the zakat funds to the recipient.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Permissible if the mosque is for poor people.
D) Impermissible only if the mosque is built for the rich.

Key Takeaway
Zakat must be given as ownership; any expenditure lacking tamlik, such as building mosques, is invalid.

Zakat for Shrouding the Dead and Debt Repayment
Ruling on zakat for shrouding the dead and debt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on using zakat for shrouding the dead and paying off the deceased's debt, and explain the exception for living persons.

Core Idea
Zakat requires ownership transfer (tamlik); the dead cannot own, so zakat cannot benefit them.

This lesson examines the first part of the passage, which prohibits the use of zakat for shrouding the deceased or paying off his debts. It highlights the principle that zakat must be given to a living recipient who can take ownership. The exception: paying the debt of a living person with his permission is valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited expenditures
Shrouding the dead and paying the debt of the deceased are explicitly prohibited.
The prohibition is because the deceased cannot own property.
2
Identify the valid expenditure
Paying the debt of a living person with his order is permissible.
This fulfills tamlik because the debtor receives ownership of the money indirectly.
3
Understand the legal basis
The rukn of zakat is tamlik (transfer of ownership), which cannot occur for a deceased person.
Hence any expenditure that does not transfer ownership to a living person is invalid.
4
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
All Hanafi imams agree on this ruling; no difference within the school.
Other schools may differ on the permissibility of paying debts without permission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ميت أي ولا تصرف إلى تكفينه ولا إلى قضاء دين الميت ولو قضى بها دين حي بأمره جاز. (ع) وشراء قن: لأن الركن في الزكاة التمليك و لم يوجد، خلافاً لمالك، حيث قال: يعتق منها الرقبة؛ لقوله تعالى: وفي الرقاب الله (البقرة: ۱۷۷)؛ ولأنه لا يجوز دفعها للمكاتب؛ لأنه عبد ما دام عليه درهم، ولنا: أن رجلا جاء إلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال: دلني على عمل يقربني إلى الجنة، ويباعدني عن النار، فقال: "أعتق النسمة، وفك الرقبة"، فقال: يا رسول الله! أو ليسا واحداً؟ قال: "لا، عتق النسمة أن تنفرد بعتقها، وفك الرقبة أن تعين في ثمنها"، والمراد بالرقاب المكاتبون أي يعانون في فك رقابهم، وهو قول جمهور العلماء. (فتح)
Shrouding the dead: i.e., zakat is not to be given for shrouding him nor for paying off the debt of the deceased. If one pays off the debt of a living person with zakat by his order, it is permissible. (ع) And buying a slave to free: because the essential element in zakat is tamlik (transfer of ownership), and it has not occurred. Contrary to Malik, who said: a slave can be freed from zakat based on the verse: 'and in freeing necks' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:177). And because it is not permissible to give zakat to a mukatab, as he is a slave as long as he owes a dirham. Our proof: A man came to the Prophet (ﷺ) and said: 'Guide me to an act that brings me close to Paradise and distances me from Fire.' He said: 'Free the soul and release the neck.' The man said: 'O Messenger of Allah, are they not the same?' He said: 'No. Freeing the soul is to free a slave solely by yourself, and releasing the neck is to help in paying his price.' The intended meaning of 'necks' are the mukatabun, i.e., they are helped in freeing their necks. This is the statement of the majority of scholars.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage covers two rulings: (1) Zakat cannot be used to shroud the dead or pay off the deceased's debt, because the deceased cannot own property. However, paying the debt of a living person with his permission is valid. (2) Zakat cannot be used to buy a slave to free, because tamlik is missing (the slave is not owned by a person who can be given ownership). The passage then shows a dispute with Imam Malik, who allows freeing slaves with zakat based on the verse 'fī al-riqāb' (in freeing necks). The Hanafi response is that 'riqāb' means mukatabun (slaves who have a contract to purchase their freedom), not purchase of an owned slave, and they provide a hadith distinguishing between freeing a slave (direct manumission) and helping a mukatab (which is by giving him money). The Hanafi position is that zakat can be given to a mukatab to help him pay his kitabah, but not to buy a slave to free. This is the majority view.

Key Terms
تمليك (tamlik): Transfer of ownership; the essential element (rukn) in zakat, without which the zakat is invalid.
ميت (mayyit): Deceased person; not eligible to receive zakat because they cannot own.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why can zakat not be used to pay off the debt of a deceased person?
A) Because the debt is not a valid category for zakat.
B) Because the deceased cannot own the money.
C) Because paying debts is not a form of charity.
D) Because it is better to use zakat for shrouding.

Key Takeaway
Zakat must reach a living owner; it cannot benefit the dead.

Zakat for Buying Slaves to Free
Prohibition of using zakat to buy slaves to free, with inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on using zakat to buy slaves to free, cite the hadith used as proof, and compare with the Maliki view.

Core Idea
Zakat cannot be used to buy a slave to free; instead, it can be given to a mukatab to help him purchase his freedom.

This lesson delves into the second ruling: the prohibition of using zakat funds to buy a slave for the purpose of manumission. The Hanafi school argues that tamlik (ownership transfer) is not achieved because the buyer owns the slave, not the slave. The passage presents a hadith distinguishing between freeing a slave directly and helping a mukatab. This contrasts with Imam Malik's view, who permits freeing slaves from zakat based on the Quranic phrase 'fī al-riqāb'. We'll analyze the proofs and the practical differences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
Zakat cannot be used to buy a slave to free because tamlik is not achieved.
The slave becomes owned by the buyer, not the slave himself.
2
Identify the Hanafi proof
The hadith where the Prophet (ﷺ) distinguishes between 'freeing the soul' (direct manumission) and 'releasing the neck' (helping a mukatab).
The hadith shows that zakat aids the second category, not the first.
3
Understand the Hanafi reasoning
Tamlik is the rukn of zakat; buying a slave does not give ownership to the slave, whereas giving money to a mukatab enables him to buy himself, fulfilling tamlik.
The mukatab is a person who owns his own earning and can receive ownership.
4
Present the Maliki view and proof
Imam Malik allows freeing any slave with zakat based on the Quranic verse 'fī al-riqāb' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:177).
Malik interprets 'riqāb' broadly to include purchasing slaves to free them.
5
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafis argue that 'riqāb' refers specifically to mukatabun, as indicated by the hadith and the majority of scholars.
Thus the verse is interpreted in light of the prophetic explanation.

Source Text

ميت أي ولا تصرف إلى تكفينه ولا إلى قضاء دين الميت ولو قضى بها دين حي بأمره جاز. (ع) وشراء قن: لأن الركن في الزكاة التمليك و لم يوجد، خلافاً لمالك، حيث قال: يعتق منها الرقبة؛ لقوله تعالى: وفي الرقاب الله (البقرة: ۱۷۷)؛ ولأنه لا يجوز دفعها للمكاتب؛ لأنه عبد ما دام عليه درهم، ولنا: أن رجلا جاء إلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال: دلني على عمل يقربني إلى الجنة، ويباعدني عن النار، فقال: "أعتق النسمة، وفك الرقبة"، فقال: يا رسول الله! أو ليسا واحداً؟ قال: "لا، عتق النسمة أن تنفرد بعتقها، وفك الرقبة أن تعين في ثمنها"، والمراد بالرقاب المكاتبون أي يعانون في فك رقابهم، وهو قول جمهور العلماء. (فتح)
Shrouding the dead: i.e., zakat is not to be given for shrouding him nor for paying off the debt of the deceased. If one pays off the debt of a living person with zakat by his order, it is permissible. (ع) And buying a slave to free: because the essential element in zakat is tamlik (transfer of ownership), and it has not occurred. Contrary to Malik, who said: a slave can be freed from zakat based on the verse: 'and in freeing necks' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:177). And because it is not permissible to give zakat to a mukatab, as he is a slave as long as he owes a dirham. Our proof: A man came to the Prophet (ﷺ) and said: 'Guide me to an act that brings me close to Paradise and distances me from Fire.' He said: 'Free the soul and release the neck.' The man said: 'O Messenger of Allah, are they not the same?' He said: 'No. Freeing the soul is to free a slave solely by yourself, and releasing the neck is to help in paying his price.' The intended meaning of 'necks' are the mukatabun, i.e., they are helped in freeing their necks. This is the statement of the majority of scholars.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage covers two rulings: (1) Zakat cannot be used to shroud the dead or pay off the deceased's debt, because the deceased cannot own property. However, paying the debt of a living person with his permission is valid. (2) Zakat cannot be used to buy a slave to free, because tamlik is missing (the slave is not owned by a person who can be given ownership). The passage then shows a dispute with Imam Malik, who allows freeing slaves with zakat based on the verse 'fī al-riqāb' (in freeing necks). The Hanafi response is that 'riqāb' means mukatabun (slaves who have a contract to purchase their freedom), not purchase of an owned slave, and they provide a hadith distinguishing between freeing a slave (direct manumission) and helping a mukatab (which is by giving him money). The Hanafi position is that zakat can be given to a mukatab to help him pay his kitabah, but not to buy a slave to free. This is the majority view.

Key Terms
رقاب (riqāb): Literally 'necks'; interpreted by Hanafis as referring to mukatab slaves, not slaves in general.
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave who has a contract with his master to purchase his freedom by paying installments.
تمليك (tamlik): Transfer of ownership; the essential element (rukn) in zakat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi proof that zakat cannot be used to buy a slave to free?
A) The Quran says 'fī al-riqāb' but does not specify buying.
B) A hadith distinguishing between direct manumission and helping a mukatab.
C) Ijma that buying slaves is not permitted.
D) Qiyas on the prohibition of selling zakat goods.

Key Takeaway
The hadith clearly separates direct manumission from helping a mukatab; zakat falls under the second, so buying slaves to free is invalid.

Zakat to Ascendants, Descendants, Spouse, and Slaves
Prohibition and dispute regarding zakat recipients.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which relatives are prohibited from receiving zakat, distinguish between the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding spouses, and apply the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Zakat cannot be given to ascendants, descendants, or slaves; the spouse's case is disputed but the mufta bihi allows wife to give to poor husband.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq outlines the prohibited recipients of zakat due to close familial or ownership ties. While there is consensus on ascendants, descendants, and slaves, the case of spouses involves an important intra-Hanafi disagreement that has practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categories
List the four categories: ascendants (even high), descendants (even low), spouses, and slaves (mukatab, mudabbir, umm walad).
Note the consensus on ascendants, descendants, and slaves; only spouses have ikhtilaf.
2
Understand the legal reasoning
The prohibition is due to the existing connection and mutual benefit between the giver and recipient, similar to the obligation of maintenance.
This is the basis for Abu Hanifa's view on spouses.
3
Compare the two positions on spouses
Abu Hanifa prohibits spouses from giving to one another. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) allow the wife to give to her poor husband, based on the hadith of Zaynab.
The hadith is about voluntary charity, but the Sahibayn apply it to zakat.
4
Evaluate the evidence
Examine the hadith of Zaynab and the different interpretations. Abu Hanifa argues that the hadith refers to voluntary sadaqah because Zaynab's jewelry was not subject to zakat in the Shafi'i school.
The tarjih (preference) in the later school is for the Sahibayn's view.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position allows a wife to give her zakat to her poor husband. A husband cannot give to his wife.
This is the easier ruling and supported by a direct hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أي لا تصرف إلى خلافا لمالك وإن علا: أي الأصل، وهم والجدات من قبل الأب والأم . (ع) وإن سفل: أي الفرع، وهم أولاد الأولاد. (ع) وزوجته: [ أي لا يدفع الزوج إلى زوجته بالاتفاق (ع)] أي لا يدفع الزكاة إلى زوجته ولو كانت معتدة من بائن أو ثلاث؛ لما بين الزوجين من الاتصال والاشتراك في المنافع؛ لوجود الاشتراك في الانتفاع عادة، فكان كالاتصال بين الأصول والفروع وهذا بالاتفاق، وكذا لا تدفع المرأة إلى زوجها وقالا: تدفع إن كان فقيرا وبه قال الشافعي؛ لحديث زينب امرأة عبد الله بن مسعود هم قالت: يا رسول الله ! إنك أمرت اليوم بالصدقة وقد كان عندي حلي فأردت أن أتصدق به فزعم ابن مسعود هو وولده أنهما أحق من تصدقت عليهم؟ فقال عليه: "صدق ابن مسعود، زوجك وولدك أحق من تصدقت عليهم"، ولأبي حنيفة ما ذكرنا من الاتصال بينهما، كان في صدقة التطوع لا الواجب ؛ لقوله عليه: "زوجك وولدك أحق والواجب لا يجوز صرفه إلى الولد؛ ولأن عند الشافعي لا تجب الزكاة في الحلي وزينب تصدقت بالكل فدل أنها كانت تطوعا. (فتح) وزوجها: أي لا تدفع الزوجة إلى زوجها عنده، وقالا: تدفع إن كان فقيراً. (مسكين) ومكاتبه: لأنه عبد ما بقي عليه درهم. [رمز الحقائق: ١٣١/١] وأم ولده : لعدم التمليك من هؤلاء الأربع، وهذا بالإجماع إلا عن أحمد في المكاتب في الأشهر. (ع)
i.e., it is not to be spent on them contrary to Malik. And (parents) even if high: i.e., the origin, they are fathers, mothers, and grandparents from the father and mother. (ع) And (children) even if low: i.e., the branch, they are children's children. (ع) And his wife: [i.e., a husband does not give to his wife by agreement] i.e., he does not give zakat to his wife, even if she is in a bain or three-fold divorce; because between the spouses there is connection and sharing of benefits; due to the existence of sharing in benefit customarily, so it is like the connection between origins and branches. This is by agreement. Similarly, a woman does not give to her husband. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say: she may give if he is poor, and al-Shafi'i also said so; based on the hadith of Zaynab, the wife of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, who said: 'O Messenger of Allah! You have commanded sadaqah today, and I had some jewelry and wanted to give it in charity, but Ibn Mas'ud claims that he and his child are more entitled to my charity?' He said: 'Ibn Mas'ud spoke the truth. Your husband and your child are more entitled to your charity.' And Abu Hanifa's proof is the connection we mentioned between them, and it was about voluntary charity, not obligatory; because the Prophet said: 'your husband and your child are more entitled,' and obligatory charity cannot be given to one's child; and because according to al-Shafi'i, zakat is not obligatory on jewelry, and Zaynab gave her jewelry entirely, which indicates it was voluntary. (Fath) And her husband: i.e., a wife does not give to her husband according to him (Abu Hanifa). But the two say: she may give if he is poor. (Miskin) And his mukatab: because he is a slave as long as a dirham remains on him. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 1/131] And his umm walad: due to the absence of tamlik from these four. This is by consensus except from Ahmad regarding the mukatab in the more famous view.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage deals with prohibited recipients due to close familial or ownership ties. (1) Ascendants: one cannot give zakat to parents, grandparents, etc., because there is a connection that negates the need for zakat (the giver is obliged to support them). (2) Descendants: similarly, own children and grandchildren are prohibited. (3) Spouses: there is a disagreement. Abu Hanifa holds that neither spouse can give zakat to the other because of the connection and mutual benefit. However, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) and al-Shafi'i allow it based on the hadith of Zaynab. Abu Hanifa interprets that hadith as applying to voluntary sadaqah, not obligatory zakat, because Zaynab's jewelry was not subject to zakat in the Shafi'i school (and Zaynab followed the Shafi'i view?). Also, he notes that the hadith says 'most entitled' which is not a clear permission for obligatory zakat. (4) Slaves: a mukatab (slave with contract to purchase freedom), mudabbir (slave promised freedom after master's death), and umm walad (slave mother of master's child) cannot receive zakat because they are still owned and tamlik to them is not possible. There is a consensus among Hanafis on these except for a minority opinion from Imam Ahmad regarding the mukatab.

Key Terms
أصل (asl): Ascendants (parents, grandparents).
فرع (far'): Descendants (children, grandchildren).
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave who has a contract to purchase his freedom.
أم ولد (umm walad): A female slave who has borne a child to her master.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, can a wife give her zakat to her poor husband?
A) No, never
B) Yes, because the husband is like a child
C) Yes, according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, it is permissible if he is poor
D) No, because the husband is an ascendant

Key Takeaway
Zakat cannot be given to ascendants, descendants, or slaves; spouses are an exception where the mufta bihi permits the wife to give to her poor husband.

Prohibited Zakat Recipients: Rich, Partially Free, and Banu Hashim
Prohibited recipients: rich, partially free slaves, and Hashimites.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on prohibited zakat recipients, identify the intra-Hanafi disagreements, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument on the rich warrior.

Core Idea
Zakat is prohibited for three categories: the nisab-owner, the partially freed slave, and Banu Hashim – with internal Hanafi nuances.

The source passage details three types of people who cannot receive zakat according to the Hanafi school. While some rulings are unanimously held, others involve disagreements within the Hanafi school (partially freed slave, Hashimi-to-Hashimi) and with the Shafi'i school (rich warrior). We'll unpack each prohibition, its evidence, and the practical fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three prohibited categories
Read the passage and list the three distinct types of recipients that the text declares impermissible to receive zakat: the partially freed slave, the rich person who owns nisab, and Banu Hashim.
2
Analyze the partial freedom ruling
Note the disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Abu Hanifa treats a partially freed slave like a mukatab (still a slave) and prohibits zakat; the Sahibayn hold that partial freedom triggers full freedom, making him eligible. Identify the mufta bihi (preferred view) as stated in the commentary.
The mufta bihi is the Sahibayn's view.
3
Examine the rich person prohibition and Shafi'i dispute
The Hanafi rule is absolute: anyone who owns nisab cannot receive zakat. Imam al-Shafi'i allows giving zakat to a rich warrior who lacks state support. Identify the Shafi'i proof (hadith of five exceptions) and the Hanafi rebuttal (weakness of that hadith or its interpretation as referring to physical strength).
Hanafis strictly uphold the general hadith forbidding sadaqah for the rich.
4
Study the Banu Hashim ruling
Zakat is prohibited for the clan of Hashim (specific families) based on the hadith 'We, the people of the household, sadaqah is not permissible for us.' Note the exclusion of Abu Lahab's descendants. Also note that voluntary sadaqah (as a gift) is allowed for them, and that the mawlas (freed slaves) of Banu Hashim are treated like them in this prohibition.
5
Resolve the intra-Hanafi dispute on Hashimi-to-Hashimi
Abu Hanifa prohibits a Hashimi from giving his zakat to another Hashimi; Abu Yusuf permits it. The mufta bihi is the view of Abu Yusuf (permissible). Understand the basis: the general prohibition does not apply between two members of the same clan.
This is a separate issue from the prohibition on receiving zakat by Hashimis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومعتق البعض: أي لا يدفع إلى عبده الذي أعتق بعضه؛ لأنه كالمكاتب عند الإمام، وعندهما: إذا أعتق بعضه كله فيصير أجنبيا. عتق عنه. (ع) وغني يملك نصاباً وفي بعض النسخ: "بملك نصاب" أي لا تدفع الزكاة إلى غني بسبب ملك نصاب مطلقاً أي نصاب كان حتى لو كان له خمس من الإبل أو أربعون من الغنم السائمة لا تحل له الصدقة، وقال الشافعي: يجوز دفع الزكاة إلى غني الغزاة إذا لم يكن له شيء في الديوان ولم يكن يأخذ من الفيء، وإنما قيد الغني بقوله: يملك نصابا؛ لأن الغني على ثلاث مراتب الأولى: ما يتعلق به وجوب الزكاة، والثانية: ما يتعلق به وجوب صدقة الفطر والأضحية، وهو ما يكون مالكاً لمقدار النصاب فاضلاً عن حوائجه الأصلية، وهو المراد هنا، والثالثة: ما يتعلق به تحريم السؤال، وهو أن يكون مالكاً لقوت يومه وما يستر به عورته عند عامة العلماء، ودليل الشافعي قوله علي: "لا تحل الصدقة لغني إلا لخمسة: الغازي في سبيل الله والعامل على الصدقات والغارم ورجل اشترى الصدقة بماله ورجل له جار مسكين تصدق عليه فأهداها للغني". ولنا: ما روينا من حديث معاذ الله وقوله عليه: "لا تحل الصدقة لغني، وما رواه لم يصح، ولئن صح فهو محمول على الغني بقوة البدن والحديث مؤول بالإجماع؛ فإنه ليس فيه تقييد بأن لا يكون له شيء في الديوان و لم يأخذ من الفيء، فإذا حمله الشافعي على هذا حملناه على ما قلنا. (فتح) وعبده وطفله: أي لا إلى عبد غني ولا إلى طفله، وقيد به؛ لأنه لو كان كبيرا فقيرا يجوز دفع الزكاة إليه وإن كان نفقته على الأب، وكذا امرأته وأبوه وطفل الغنية إذا كانوا فقراء يجوز الدفع إليهم. (مسكين) وبني هاشم أي لا يجوز دفع الزكاة إلى بني هاشم لخبر البخاري: "نحن أهل بيت لا تحل لنا الصدقة"، وبنو هاشم آل علي وعباس وجعفر وعقيل وحارث بن عبد المطلب، وخصوا بالذكر؛ لأن بعض بني هاشم يعني بنى أبي لهب يجوز دفع الزكاة إليهم؛ لأن حرمة الصدقة كرامة لهم، وإنما استحقوها لنصرتهم النبي عليه في الجاهلية والإسلام ثم سرى ذلك إلى أولادهم، وأبو لهب آذى النبي الله فلا يستحق الكرامة، وكذا لا تدفع إلى موالي بني هاشم أي معتقيهم لما روي أنه علي بعث رجلاً من بني مخزوم على الصدقة فقال الرجل لأبي رافع مولى رسول الله : أصحبني كي ما يصيبك منها؟ فقال: حتى أسأل رسول الله له فانطلق فسأله فقال علي: "إن الصدقة لا تحل لنا، وإن مولى القوم من "أنفسهم" أي في حل الصدقة وحرمتها لا من جميع الوجوه، ألا ترى أنه ليس بكفء لهم وأن مولى المسلم إذا كان كافرا تؤخذ منه الجزية، ومولى التغلبي لا تؤخذ منه المضاعفة، ولا فرق الصدقة الواجبة والتطوع، وكذا الوقف لا يحل لهم، وقال بعض أصحابنا يحل لهم التطوع على وجه الصلة، والهاشمي لا يجوز له أن يدفع زكاته إلى هاشمي مثله عند أبي حنيفة خلافاً لأبي يوسف. (فتح، مستخلص) مواليهم: أي معتق بني هاشم، ويجوز النفل لهم على وجه الصلة. (ط،ع)
And the partially freed slave: i.e., he does not give to his slave who is partially freed; because he is like a mukatab according to Imam (Abu Hanifa). According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), when a part of a slave is freed, it is all freed, so he becomes a stranger; the part is freed from him. (ع) And the rich person who owns a nisab: in some copies 'with ownership of nisab' i.e., zakat is not given to a rich person due to ownership of a nisab absolutely, whatever nisab it is; even if he has five camels or forty grazing sheep, sadaqah is not permissible for him. Al-Shafi'i said: It is permissible to give zakat to a wealthy warrior if he has nothing in the diwan and does not take from the fay'. He restricted the rich to one who owns nisab because wealth is of three levels: the first: what makes zakat obligatory; the second: what makes fitrah and udhiyah obligatory, which is owning a nisab beyond basic needs; and this is what is meant here; the third: what makes asking prohibited, which is owning food for a day and covering one's nakedness according to most scholars. The proof of al-Shafi'i is the hadith: 'Sadaqah is not permissible for a rich person except for five: the warrior in the path of Allah, the zakat collector, the bankrupt, a person who buys sadaqah with his money, and a person who has a poor neighbor who gave him sadaqah and then he gifted it to the rich.' Our proof is the hadith we narrated from Mu'adh (?) and his saying: 'Sadaqah is not permissible for the rich.' And what he narrated is not authentic, and even if it is authentic, it is interpreted as referring to the rich in physical strength, and the hadith is interpreted by consensus; for there is no restriction in it that he has nothing in the diwan and does not take from the fay'. So if al-Shafi'i interprets it as such, we interpret it as we said. (Fath) And his slave and his child: i.e., not to a rich slave nor to his child. It is restricted because if it were an adult poor, it is permissible to give him zakat even if his father supports him. Similarly, his wife, his father, and the child of a rich woman if they are poor, it is permissible to give to them. (Miskin) And Banu Hashim: i.e., it is not permissible to pay zakat to Banu Hashim due to the report of al-Bukhari: 'We, the people of the household, sadaqah is not permissible for us.' Banu Hashim are the families of Ali, Abbas, Ja'far, Aqil, and Harith ibn Abd al-Muttalib. They are specifically mentioned because some of Banu Hashim, meaning the children of Abu Lahab, it is permissible to pay zakat to them; because the prohibition of sadaqah is an honor for them, and they earned it for supporting the Prophet in Jahiliyyah and Islam, and it passes to their children. Abu Lahab harmed the Prophet, so he does not deserve the honor. Similarly, zakat is not paid to the mawlas of Banu Hashim, i.e., their freed slaves, due to the report that Ali sent a man from Banu Makhzum to collect sadaqah, and the man said to Abu Rafi', the freed slave of the Prophet: 'Accompany me so that you may get something from it?' He said: 'Let me ask the Messenger of Allah.' He went and asked, and he (the Prophet) said: 'Sadaqah is not permissible for us, and the freed slave of a people is from themselves' i.e., in the permissibility and prohibition of sadaqah, not in all aspects. Do you not see that he is not their equal and that the freed slave of a Muslim, if he is a disbeliever, is subject to jizyah, and the freed slave of a Taghlabi does not have the double tax? There is no difference between obligatory sadaqah and voluntary. Similarly, waqf is not permissible for them. Some of our companions said: voluntary (nafl) is permissible for them as a gift. A Hashimi cannot give his zakat to another Hashimi like himself according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to Abu Yusuf. (Fath, Mustakhlas) Their mawlas: i.e., the freed slaves of Banu Hashim, and voluntary charity is permissible for them as a gift.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage discusses three more prohibited recipients. (1) A slave who is partially freed: According to Abu Hanifa, he is like a mukatab and cannot receive zakat. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, if a part is freed, the whole becomes free, so he is a stranger and can receive zakat. (2) A rich person who owns a nisab: Zakat cannot be given to him. The definition of 'rich' here is one who owns a nisab beyond basic needs. Al-Shafi'i allows giving zakat to a warrior rich in physical strength but poor in wealth, citing a hadith about five exceptions. The Hanafi response is that the correct hadith absolutely forbids sadaqah for the rich, and the Shafi'i hadith is either weak or interpreted as referring to a different context. (3) Banu Hashim: They cannot receive zakat due to a hadith. This includes the families of Ali, Abbas, Ja'far, Aqil, and Harith, but excludes the children of Abu Lahab because he did not support the Prophet. Also, the mawlas (freed slaves) of Banu Hashim are treated like them in prohibition of zakat. There is a further intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa says a Hashimi cannot give his zakat to another Hashimi, but Abu Yusuf allows it. Voluntary sadaqah is allowed for them as a gift (hadiyya).

Key Terms
بني هاشم (Bani Hashim): The clan of the Prophet Muhammad (ﷺ), including the descendants of Hashim. Specifically, the families of Ali, Abbas, Ja'far, Aqil, and Harith.
معتق البعض (mu'taq al-ba'd): A slave who has been partially freed; a person who has some share of freedom but not all.
الغني (al-ghani): The rich person; in this context, one who owns a nisab beyond basic needs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school, can a Hashimi give his zakat to another Hashimi?
A) No, it is prohibited because Banu Hashim cannot receive zakat.
B) Yes, it is permissible according to Abu Yusuf's view, which is the mufta bihi.
C) No, because the zakat must be given to non-Hashimis only.
D) Yes, but only if the recipient is poor.

Key Takeaway
Zakat cannot be given to a nisab-owner, a partially freed slave (according to the stronger view it is allowed), or to Banu Hashim, with the exception that voluntary charity (as a gift) is permitted for them.
