Fitrana for Dependents: The Hanafi Condition of Wilāyah
States obligations and exemptions for paying fitrana for family members

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on fitrana for dependents and apply the sabab (maintenance and guardianship) to determine obligation.

Core Idea
Fitrana is wajib for those you maintain and have guardianship over — not for your wife or adult child.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqā'iq explains the Hanafi rules for who must be covered by one's fitrana payment. Unlike the Shafi'i school, the Hanafis require both maintenance (nafaqah) and guardianship (wilāyah) for the obligation to apply. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly fulfilling this wajib duty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its hukm
Confirm that fitrana (ṣadaqat al-fiṭr) is classified as wajib in the Hanafi school, not fard, due to its zanni proof.
The passage does not explicitly state this, but it is implicit from the context; recall the usul principle that ahad hadith yields wujub.
2
List those for whom fitrana is wajib
From the passage, enumerate the dependents: poor minor child, service slaves, mudabbar, and umm walad.
Service slaves are those used for household work, not trade.
3
List those for whom fitrana is not wajib
Identify the exclusions: wife, adult child (unless insane), mukatab, and trade slaves.
Trade slaves are excluded to avoid double taxation.
4
Understand the cause (sabab) of obligation
The obligation requires both providing maintenance (nafaqah) and having legal guardianship (wilāyah). The wife and adult child lack the latter, so they are excluded.
For the insane adult child, guardianship continues, so fitrana is wajib.
5
Analyze the proofs and inter-madhhab dispute
The Hanafi proof includes the hadith from Ali: 'Pay for every free and slave', and the prohibition of double taxation. The Shafi'i argument from 'Pay for those you support' is specified by the Hanafis with the condition of wilāyah.
Note the intra-Hanafi disagreement with Muhammad regarding the wealthy child.

باب صدقة الفطر

وعبد أو عبيد لهما، ويتوقف

أي لا تجب عن

الصغير

يتحملها المولى، والكافر ليس بأهل، ولنا: إطلاق قوله عليا: أدوا عن كل حر وعبد، فلا يشترط فيه إسلام العبد كالزكاة، ولا تجب عن عبيد للتجارة؛ لأن إيجابها يؤدي إلى الثني، وهو لا يجوز؛ لقوله عليه: "لا ثني في الصدقة" أي لا تؤخذ السنة مرتين. (فتح) الفقير: يعني أولاده الصغار الفقراء، فإن كان طفله غنيا يجب في ماله خلافاً لمحمد. (ع) وعبيده: أي عن عبيد الخدمة لا للتجارة خلافاً للشافعي (ع) أم ولده لما روى الدار قطني أنه عليه أمر بصدقة الفطر عن والكبير والحر والعبد ممن تمونون، وهؤلاء المذكورون بهذه الصفة على الكمال. (ع) لا عن زوجته لأنه لا يلي عليها ولا يمونها إلا لضرورة نظام مصالح النكاح، ولهذا لا يجب عليه غير الرواتب نحو الأدوية، وقوله: وولده الكبير؛ لأنه لا يمونه ولا يلي عليه، فانعدم السبب، وكذا إن كان في عياله لعدم الولاية عليه، إلا أن يكون مجنونا، ولو أدى عن الزوجة والولد الكبير جاز استحساناً؛ لثبوت الإذن عادة، ولا يؤدي عن أجداده وجداته؛ لأنهم ليسوا في معنى نفسه خلافاً للشافعي فيهما أي في الزوجة والولد الكبير؛ لقوله عليه: "أدوا عن من تمونون"، ولنا ما سبق من أ أن السبب رأس يمونه ويلي عليه ولا ولاية له عليهما. (فتح)
Chapter of Fitrana. And his poor child, and his slaves for service, and his mudabbar, and his umm walad – not for his wife and adult child and mukatab – i.e., it is not obligatory on the man. And a slave or slaves belonging to both, and it is suspended. Shared between two, jointly between them, i.e., the obligation of fitrana. i.e., it is not obligatory for the minor, the master bears it. The disbeliever is not qualified. Our proof: the absolute statement of Ali: 'Pay for every free and slave', so Islam of the slave is not required, like zakat. It is not obligatory for slaves for trade because it would lead to double taxation, which is not allowed due to his statement: 'No double taxation in sadaqah' i.e., the sunnah is not taken twice. (Fath) Al-Faqir: meaning his poor minor children; if his child is wealthy, it is obligatory from his wealth, contrary to Muhammad. (Ayni) And his slaves: i.e., for service slaves, not for trade, contrary to al-Shafi'i. (Ayni) Umm walad: because al-Daraqutni narrated that he ordered fitrana for, and the adult, and the free, and the slave from those whom you support, and these mentioned are in this description completely. (Ayni) Not for his wife because he has no guardianship over her nor does he support her except for necessity of the system of marital benefits; thus non-routine expenses like medicine are not obligatory on him. And his statement: 'his adult child' because he does not support him nor has guardianship over him, so the cause is absent. Similarly, even if he is in his household due to lack of guardianship, unless he is insane. If he pays for the wife and adult child, it is permissible by istihsan due to customary permission. He does not pay for his grandfathers and grandmothers because they are not in the sense of himself, contrary to al-Shafi'i regarding both (wife and adult child) due to his statement: 'Pay for those you support.' Our proof: what preceded that the cause is a head whom he supports and has guardianship over, and he has no guardianship over both. (Fath)
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqā'iq, with commentaries from al-ʿAynī and Fatḥ al-Qadīr, explains who a man must pay fitrana for. The basic Hanafi rule: fitrana is wajib for those he both provides maintenance (nafaqah) for and has guardianship (wilāyah) over. Thus it is wajib for his poor minor children, his slaves for service (not trade), his mudabbar (slave promised freedom upon master's death), and his umm walad (slave mother of his child). It is not wajib for his wife because the husband has no guardianship over her (she is independent), nor for his adult child (even if living with him) because he no longer maintains him, unless the adult child is insane. If he pays for them anyway, it's valid by istihsan due to customary permission. The Shafi'i school argues from the hadith 'Pay for those you support' that fitrana is wajib for all dependents including wife and adult child. The Hanafi response is that the sabab (cause) is both maintenance and guardianship; the wife and adult child lack the latter. The passage also notes that fitrana is not wajib for trade slaves because it would lead to double taxation (thani), prohibited by hadith. It also mentions a disagreement with Muhammad al-Shaybani regarding a wealthy child: Muhammad says it's wajib from the child's own wealth, while Abu Hanifa says it's on the father.

Key Terms
صدقة الفطر (ṣadaqat al-fiṭr): A wajib charity given at the end of Ramadan per head, required for every free Muslim who owns the nisab.
ولاية (wilāyah): Legal guardianship over a person, which the husband does not have over his wife in Hanafi fiqh regarding fitrana.
ثني (thaniy): Double taxation; taking sadaqah twice in one year from the same property, prohibited by hadith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, why is fitrana not wajib for the wife?
A) Because she is not a dependent
B) Because the husband has no guardianship (wilāyah) over her
C) Because she has her own wealth
D) Because the Prophet explicitly exempted her

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, fitrana for dependents requires both maintenance and guardianship; hence wife and adult child are not covered.

Fitrana for Jointly Owned Slaves and Slaves Purchased with Option
Two rulings on fitrana for incomplete ownership

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for fitrana on a jointly owned slave and on a slave under option, and explain the underlying rationale regarding ownership and guardianship.

Core Idea
Incomplete ownership means no fitrana; suspended ownership means fitrana awaits final ownership.

Fitrana is wajib upon the master for each slave he fully owns. But what if the slave is owned jointly, or the sale is still pending? This lesson explains two special cases where ownership is incomplete or suspended, and the disputes surrounding them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first case: jointly owned slave
State the Hanafi position that fitrana is not wajib on either partner. Note the reason: lack of complete guardianship and maintenance.
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute with the Sahibayn regarding multiple slaves.
2
Understand the Sahibayn's view for multiple jointly owned slaves
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that each partner pays for complete slaves according to his share, ignoring fractions. For example, five slaves shared equally means each pays for two.
They consider partition (qismah) effective.
3
Explain the rationale behind Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa does not enforce partition of slaves, so ownership remains undivided; thus, no fitrana is obligable.
This is the relied-upon position.
4
Identify the second case: slave purchased with option
If Ramadan ends while the option period remains, fitrana is suspended until ownership is determined. It falls on the one to whom ownership is finally established.
Unlike maintenance, which is immediate.
5
Distinguish fitrana from maintenance
Maintenance is for immediate need and thus cannot be suspended. Fitrana is based on ownership, which is suspended during the option period.
Zufar and al-Shafi'i hold different views.

وعبد أو عبيد :لهما أما العبد المشترك فلا تجب عنه عندنا على أحد من الشريكين؛ لقصور الولاية والمؤنة في حق كل واحد من السيدين وفيه خلاف الشافعي بناء على أصله من أنها تجب على العبد ابتداء ثم يتحملها المولى عنه، والعبد ههنا كامل في نفسه وهما يمونانه فتجب عليهما، وأما العبيد المشتركة فعندهما على كل واحد منهما ما يخصه من الرؤوس دون الأشقاص حتى لو كان بينهما خمسة أعبد يجب على كل واحد منهما الصدقة عن عبدين؛ لأنه باعتبار القسمة يكون ملك كل واحد من السيدين كاملا في عبدين ولا يعتبر النصف الخامس، والأصل في هذا أن الإمام لا يرى قسمة الرقيق وهما يريانها يعني أ أن أبا حنيفة لا یری قسمة الرقيق جبراً فلا يملك كل واحد منهما عبداً معينا، بل ملكهما شائع في الكل، وقيل: لا تجب إجماعا؛ لأن النصيب لا يجتمع قبل القسمة فلم تتم . الرقبة بواحد منهما. (فتح)

ويتوقف إلخ أي لو اشترى عبدا بالخيار ومر وقت الفطر، والخيار باق ففطرته على من يستقر الملك له، بخلاف النفقة فإنها تجب على من كان له الملك وقت الوجوب لعدم احتمالها التوقف؛ لأنها تجب لحاجة المملوك للحال، فلو جعلناها موقوفا لمات جوعا وعند زفر على من له الخيار ؛ لأن الولاية له، وقال الشافعي على من له الملك وقت الوجوب كالنفقة ولنا أن الملك موقوف؛ لأنه لو رد يعود إلى قديم ملك البائع، ولو أجيز يثبت الملك للمشتري من وقت العقد فيتوقف ما يبتني عليه بخلاف النفقة فإنها للحال الناجزة فلا تقبل التوقف. (فتح)
And a slave or slaves: between them. As for the common slave, it is not obligatory upon either of the two partners in our view, due to lack of guardianship and maintenance in the right of each master; and there is the disagreement of al-Shafi'i built on his principle that it is obligatory on the slave initially then the master bears it, and the slave here is complete in himself and they both support him so it is obligatory on them. As for jointly owned slaves, according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) each one owes what is specific to him of the heads without fractions, such that if they share five slaves, each one owes sadaqah for two slaves, because by partition the ownership of each master becomes complete in two slaves, and the half of the fifth is not considered. The basis of this is that the Imam (Abu Hanifa) does not consider partition of slaves, while they consider it, meaning Abu Hanifa does not see forced partition of slaves, so each does not own a specific slave, but their ownership is shared in the whole. It is said it is not obligatory by consensus because the share does not unite before partition, so the neck (ownership of the slave) is not complete for either. (Fath)

And 'it is suspended' etc., meaning if one buys a slave with option and the time of fitr passes while the option remains, then his fitrana is on the one to whom ownership is finally established, unlike maintenance which is obligatory on whoever had ownership at the time of obligation, because maintenance does not bear suspension; because it is for the immediate need of the slave, so if we made it suspended he might die of hunger. According to Zufar, it is on the one who has the option because guardianship is his. Al-Shafi'i said it is on the one who has ownership at the time of obligation, like maintenance. Our proof: ownership is suspended because if he returns (the slave), it goes back to the seller's previous ownership, and if he confirms, ownership is established for the buyer from the time of contract, so what is based upon it is suspended, unlike maintenance which is for an immediate need and does not admit suspension. (Fath)
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqā'iq with Fatḥ al-Qadīr commentary addresses two special cases of slavery. First, a slave jointly owned by two masters (ʿabd mushtarak). The Hanafi position: fitrana is not wajib on either partner. The reason: neither has full guardianship nor full maintenance responsibility—each has only a share. Al-Shafi'i disagrees, holding that fitrana is originally on the slave, and the master bears it; here the slave is complete and both support him, so it's wajib on both. The commentary then addresses multiple jointly owned slaves: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that each master pays for the number of complete slaves his share amounts to, ignoring fractions. For example, if they share five slaves, each owns two and a half, so each pays for two. Abu Hanifa does not consider partition (qismah) in this ruling because he does not enforce partition of slaves; thus ownership is undivided, so no fitrana is wajib on either. The second case: a slave purchased with an option (khiyār). If Ramadan ends while the option period still runs, fitrana is suspended until ownership is determined: if the sale is finalized, the buyer pays; if rescinded, the seller pays. This differs from maintenance (nafaqah), which is wajib immediately on whoever has ownership at the moment, because maintenance is for urgent need. Zufar and al-Shafi'i hold alternative views: Zufar puts it on the party holding the option because he has guardianship; al-Shafi'i puts it on the owner at the time of obligation, analogizing to maintenance. The Hanafi response relies on the suspended nature of ownership during the option period.

Key Terms
عبد مشترك (ʿabd mushtarak): A slave jointly owned by two or more masters, with undivided ownership.
خيار (khiyār): An option in a sales contract allowing a party to cancel or confirm the sale within a specified period.
قسمة الرقيق (qismat al-raqīq): Division of slaves among co-owners; Abu Hanifa does not enforce it while the Sahibayn do.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is fitrana not obligatory on either partner for a jointly owned slave?
A) Because the slave is not fully owned by either
B) Because neither has complete guardianship and maintenance
C) Because the slave cannot be forced to pay
D) Because they both can rely on the other to pay

Key Takeaway
Fitrana for a slave hinges on complete ownership; incomplete or suspended ownership either removes or suspends the obligation.

Types and Quantities of Fitrana and the Measure of the Sa'
Specifies the types and quantities of food for fitrana and the weight of the sa'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the types and quantities of fitrana, identify the measure of the sa' as eight Baghdadi ratls, and explain the intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab disputes regarding raisins and the sa' weight.

Core Idea
Fitrana requires half a sa' of wheat or one sa' of dates/barley; the Hanafi sa' is 8 Baghdadi ratls.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq specifies the obligatory food types and quantities for zakat al-fitr. It also defines the measure of the sa' and addresses disputes with Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i. Understanding these details is crucial for correctly fulfilling the wajib of fitrana.

Guided Path
1
Identify the obligatory categories and amounts
Read the passage to list the types of food (wheat, barley, dates, raisins, flour, sawiq) and the required quantity (half sa' or full sa').
Note that wheat and its derivatives require half a sa', while barley and dates require a full sa'.
2
Understand the base measure: the sa'
Note the explicit definition: the sa' is eight Baghdadi ratls. Recognize that each ratl is 20 ustars, and each ustar is 4.5 mithqals.
This is Abu Hanifa's position, supported by the hadith of Anas.
3
Analyze the dispute on raisins
Compare Abu Hanifa's view (half sa', like wheat) with Abu Yusuf and Muhammad's view (one sa', like barley). Observe the reasoning based on fruit consumption and waste.
The mufta bihi is the opinion of the Sahibayn (one sa').
4
Evaluate the sa' weight dispute with Shafi'i
Examine the Shafi'i evidence ('Our sa' is the smallest') and the Hanafi counter-evidence (hadith of Anas). Also note Abu Yusuf's reported retraction.
The Hanafi position of 8 ratls remains authoritative for fatwa.

(ع) نصف صاع بالرفع . أي الصدقة نصف صاع (ع) دقيقه أو سويقه: أطلق الدقيق فشمل الجيد والرديء، ودقيق البر وسويقه كالبر و لم يذكرهما من الشعير ولا حكمهما، فاعلم أن دقيق الشعير وسويقه كالشعير حتى يجب من كل واحد منهما الصاع والأولى أن يراعى فيهما القدر والقيمة احتياطاً؛ لضعف الآثار فيهما، وقالا : الزبيب كالشعير؛ لأن الزبيب يقارب التمر من حيث المقصود وهو التفكه، وللإمام ما روي في الخبر: "أو نصف صاع من زبيب؛ ولأنه والبر يتقاربان؛ لأن كل واحد منهما يوكل بجميع أجزائه، ولا يرمي البر النخالة . من الزبيب الحب إلا المترفهون بخلاف التمر والشعير فإنه يرمى منهما النوى والنخالة، وبه ظهر التفاوت بين التمر والبر وقال الشافعي من الكل صاع ولا يجزئ نصف صاع من بر بقول أبي سعيد الخدري: "كنا نخرج على عهد رسول الله الا الله صاعاً من طعام أو صاعاً من شعير أو صاعاً . أو صاعاً من زبيب"، وفي بعض طرقه ذكر "صاعاً من دقيق"، ولنا: قوله عليها في خطبته: "أدوا عن كل حر أو عبد، ولا من ! منهم أحد أقط من الخلفاء منهم أن صغير أو كبير نصف صاع من بر"، وروى الحاكم في "المستدرك" عن ابن عمر لهما عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه أمر عمرو بن حزم في زكاة الفطر بنصف صاع من حنطة أو صاع من تمر، وهو مذهب جمهور الصحابة، الراشدون وابن مسعود وابن عباس وابن الزبير وجابر وغيرهم من كبار الصحابة ، ولم يرو عن نصف صاع من بر لا يجزئ فكان إجماعاً، وحديث الخدري محمول على أنهم كانوا يتبرعون بالزيادة وكلامنا في الوجوب، وليس فيه دلالة على أنه علي عرف ذلك منهم فلا يلزم حجة. [تبيين الحقائق: ۱۳۷/۲] (عيني، فتح) أو سويقه: وهو البر المقلو، وقال الشافعي: لا يجوز منهما. (ع)

أو زبيب : أي أو نصف صاع أيضاً من زبيب وقال الزبيب كالشعير و به يفتى. The amount of fitrana. [??] and if sold with option, half a sa' of wheat or its flour or its sawiq (parched barley) or raisins, or a sa' of dates or if the owned (slave) is barley, and it is eight ratls. i.e., the sa' by Baghdadi measure according to both parties. And it is wheat i.e., flour of wheat. i.e., or it is obligatory. With option for one or both, so when the time of fitr passes and the option remains, it is obligatory on the one to whom the slave becomes, meaning if the sale is completed then on the buyer, and if rescinded then on the seller. (Ayni) Half a sa' in the nominative, i.e., the sadaqah is half a sa'. (Ayni) 'Or its flour or sawiq': he mentioned flour generally covering good and bad, and flour of wheat and its sawiq are like wheat; he did not mention them for barley nor their ruling. Know that flour of barley and its sawiq are like barley so that a sa' is obligatory from each of them, and it is better to consider quantity and value precautionarily due to weak reports on them. They (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: raisins are like barley because raisins approximate dates in purpose which is consumption as fruit; and for the Imam (Abu Hanifa) it is narrated in the report: 'Or half a sa' of raisins' and because it and wheat are close, since each is eaten with all its parts, and wheat does not discard bran except by the luxurious, unlike dates and barley which discard pits and bran; thus the difference between dates and wheat appears. Al-Shafi'i said: from all one sa', and half a sa' of wheat is not sufficient, based on the statement of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: 'We used to give in the time of the Prophet a sa' of food or a sa' of barley or a sa' of raisins'; and in some of its paths 'a sa' of flour' is mentioned. Our proof: his statement in his sermon: 'Pay for every free or slave, young or old, half a sa' of wheat'. And al-Hakim narrated in al-Mustadrak from Ibn Umar that the Prophet instructed Amr ibn Hazm regarding zakat al-fitr: half a sa' of wheat or a sa' of dates. This is the madhhab of the majority of the Companions: the righteous caliphs, Ibn Mas'ud, Ibn Abbas, Ibn al-Zubayr, Jabir, and other senior Companions. And there is no report that half a sa' of wheat does not suffice, so it is a consensus. The hadith of al-Khudri is interpreted as them voluntarily giving extra, for our discussion is about obligation, and it does not indicate that the Prophet knew of that, so it is not a proof. (Ayni, Fath) 'Or sawiq' which is roasted wheat; al-Shafi'i said it is not permissible from either. (Ayni) 'Or raisins': i.e., also half a sa' of raisins, and it is said raisins are like barley, and it is the fatwa. (Ayni) 'And it is eight ratls': each ratl is twenty ustars, and the ustar - with kasra on the hamza - is four and a half mithqals. Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i said: the sa' is five and one-third ratls, based on his statement: 'Our sa' is the smallest of sa's'. It is narrated that when Abu Yusuf performed Hajj, he asked the people of Madinah about the sa', and they said five and one-third ratls, and a group came each with his sa', some saying my father told me it is the sa' of the Prophet, some saying my brother told me it is his sa', so Abu Yusuf retracted his view. Our proof: what the author of al-Imam narrated in Sharh al-Ilmam that Anas said: he (the Prophet) performed wudu with a mudd of two ratls, and ghusl with a sa' of eight ratls. It is said there is no difference among them; rather Abu Yusuf, when he measured the sa' of the people of Madinah, found the sa' to be five and one-third ratls.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage is the core of Kanz al-Daqā'iq on the amount of fitrana, with detailed commentary from al-ʿAynī and Fatḥ al-Qadīr. The Hanafi position: the obligatory amount is either half a sa' of wheat (or its flour or sawiq) or half a sa' of raisins, or one full sa' of dates or barley. The sa' is defined as eight Baghdadi ratls (approx. 3.2 kg). Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i hold that the sa' is five and one-third ratls, based on the hadith 'Our sa' is the smallest of sa's' and local practice in Madinah. Abu Hanifa's proof includes the hadith of Anas that the Prophet's sa' for ghusl was eight ratls. The passage also discusses equivalencies: flour and sawiq of wheat are treated as wheat (half sa'), while flour and sawiq of barley are treated as barley (full sa'). Raisins are treated like barley according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, but Abu Hanifa holds they are like wheat because they are eaten whole without discarding. The inter-madhhab dispute with al-Shafi'i: al-Shafi'i requires one sa' of any food, citing Abu Sa'id al-Khudri. Hanafi responds that the hadith of Amr ibn Hazm and the practice of the majority of Companions support half a sa' of wheat, and the other hadith is interpreted as voluntary excess. The passage also repeats the rule for a slave sold with option: fitrana depends on final ownership.

Key Terms
صاع (ṣāʿ): A measure of volume; in Hanafi fiqh for fitrana, it is eight Baghdadi ratls (approx. 3.2 kg).
رطل (raṭl): A unit of weight; Baghdadi ratl = 20 ustars ≈ 406.25 g (different from the later Egyptian ratl).
زبيب (zabīb): Raisins, considered by Abu Hanifa as equivalent to wheat (half sa'), but by Abu Yusuf and Muhammad as equivalent to barley (one sa').

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the Hanafi position on the measure of the sa' for fitrana?
A) Five and one-third ratls
B) Eight Baghdadi ratls
C) Four ratls
D) Six ratls

Key Takeaway
Fitrana requires half a sa' of wheat or one sa' of dates/barley; the Hanafi sa' is eight Baghdadi ratls, a position supported by the hadith of Anas and the practice of the Companions.

Zakat — Almsgiving

Prescribed Items and Amounts for Zakat al-Fitr
Inter-madhhab dispute with intra-Hanafi details

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the obligatory items and amounts for Zakat al-Fitr, distinguish the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on raisins, and evaluate the Hanafi proof against al-Shafi'i's view.

Core Idea
Half a sa‘ of wheat suffices; the fatwa on raisins is a full sa‘.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq and its commentary addresses the prescribed items and amounts for Zakat al-Fitr. It is a classic inter-madhhab dispute: the Hanafi school holds that half a sa‘ of wheat (and its derivatives) fulfills the obligation, while al-Shafi'i requires a full sa‘ from all items. The passage also reveals an intra-Hanafi difference on raisins, with the fatwa settling on the view of the Two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Understanding these rulings requires careful attention to the proofs and the hierarchy of evidence.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on prescribed items
Identify the items mentioned in the matn: wheat, flour, sawiq, raisins (half sa‘); dates, barley (full sa‘). Note that the sa‘ is the Baghdadi measure of eight ratls.
The quantities differ by grain — not all are half or full.
2
Identify the opposing school and their proof
Al-Shafi'i argues that a full sa‘ is required from all items, including wheat. His primary proof is the hadith of Abu Sa‘id al-Khudri reporting a sa‘ of food.
This is a key proof for the Shafi'i position.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school responds with stronger textual evidence: the Prophet's explicit sermon commanding half a sa‘ of wheat, the practice of the Rightly-Guided Caliphs, and the consensus of many Companions. The hadith of Abu Sa‘id is interpreted as voluntary extra giving, not the obligatory minimum.
The Hanafi position relies on multiple lines of evidence.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: according to Hanafi, giving half a sa‘ of wheat is valid; according to Shafi'i, it is not sufficient and must be completed.
This difference has real implications for the validity of the act.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on raisins
Imam Abu Hanifa held that half a sa‘ of raisins is sufficient (based on a hadith), while the Two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) analogize raisins to barley, requiring a full sa‘. The fatwa follows the Two.
The fiqh hierarchy: the mufta bihi is the view of the Sahibayn.

Chapter of Zakat al-Fitr. Prescribed amount of Zakat al-Fitr: ... half a sa' of wheat, or its flour, or its sawiq, or raisins, or a sa' of dates, or barley if the slave is owned. And it is eight ratls. Explanation: the sa' according to the two parties (Abu Hanifa and the two) is the Baghdadi sa'. 'It' refers to wheat, i.e., flour of wheat. ... The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: raisins are like barley; because raisins are similar to dates in purpose which is eating for pleasure. And for the Imam (Abu Hanifa) is what is narrated in the hadith: 'or half a sa' of raisins'; and because they and wheat are similar, as each is eaten with all its parts, and the husk of wheat is not thrown away, unlike dates and barley. ... Al-Shafi'i said: from everything a sa' is obligatory and a half sa' of wheat is not sufficient, based on the saying of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: 'We used to give during the time of the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, a sa' of food, or a sa' of barley, or a sa' of raisins.' And in some of its chains: 'a sa' of flour.' Our proof: his saying, peace be upon him, in his sermon: 'Give for every free or slave, young or old, half a sa' of wheat.' And al-Hakim narrated in al-Mustadrak from Ibn Umar that the Messenger ordered Amr ibn Hazm in Zakat al-Fitr to give half a sa' of wheat or a sa' of dates. And this is the way of the majority of Companions, the rightly-guided caliphs, Ibn Mas'ud, Ibn Abbas, Ibn al-Zubayr, Jabir, and other great Companions. And it is not narrated that half a sa' of wheat is not sufficient, so it is consensus. And the hadith of al-Khudri is interpreted that they were giving extra voluntarily; our discussion is about obligation. ... Or sawiq: it is roasted wheat, and al-Shafi'i says both (sawiq and flour) are not permissible. Or raisins: meaning also half a sa' of raisins, and the view that raisins are like barley is the fatwa.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the obligatory amount of wheat (burr) for Zakat al-Fitr, along with intra-Hanafi differences on raisins (zabib). The author first presents the matn stating the prescribed items: half a sa' of wheat, its flour, its sawiq (roasted wheat), or raisins; or a full sa' of dates or barley. The commentary clarifies that the sa' is the Baghdadi measure (eight ratls). It then explains the rulings for flour and sawiq: those of wheat follow wheat (half sa'), while those of barley follow barley (full sa'). The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider raisins like barley, requiring a full sa', due to similarity with dates. Imam Abu Hanifa, based on a hadith, permits half a sa' of raisins. The author then details the main dispute with al-Shafi'i, who requires a full sa' from all items, including wheat. Al-Shafi'i's proof is the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri reporting a sa' of food. The Hanafi response cites stronger evidence: the Prophet's explicit sermon commanding half a sa' of wheat, the practice of the Rightly-Guided Caliphs and many Companions, and the consensus (ijma) that half a sa' suffices. The hadith of al-Khudri is interpreted as voluntary extra giving, not the obligatory minimum. The fatwa (mufta bihi) on raisins follows the view of the two (full sa'). This passage teaches the importance of textual evidence over analogy in determining worship obligations.

Key Terms
صاع (sa'): A measure of volume used for Zakat al-Fitr; here defined as 8 ratls (Baghdadi) or 5⅓ ratls (Madani) according to other views.
بر (burr): Wheat, the best quality grain for Zakat al-Fitr; half a sa' is required.
زبيب (zabib): Raisins; subject to dispute: Abu Hanifa says half sa', Abu Yusuf & Muhammad say full sa' (like barley).

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Two sa'

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires half a sa' of wheat (and its derivatives) for Zakat al-Fitr, while a full sa' is required for dates, barley, and raisins (the latter per the fatwa).

Time of Obligation for Zakat al-Fitr: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Determines the time of obligation for Zakat al-Fitr and discusses prepayment and delay.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the time of wujub for Zakat al-Fitr, explain the linguistic proof, and distinguish it from the Shafi'i position. You will also be able to identify the correct view on prepayment and delay.

Core Idea
Zakat al-Fitr becomes wajib at fajr of Eid day, not sunset—the Day of Fitr is named for the day, not the night.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses a key inter-madhhab dispute: when exactly does Zakat al-Fitr become obligatory? The Hanafi school ties it to the dawn of Eid al-Fitr, while the Shafi'i school ties it to the sunset of the last day of Ramadan. The text also explores the scope for prepayment and delay, settling intra-Hanafi disagreements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
State the time of wujub according to the Hanafi school. The matn says: 'The morning of the day of Fitr.' This means fajr of Eid day.
This is the foundation of the lesson.
2
Analyse the Hanafi Proof
Examine the linguistic argument: the phrase 'Day of Fitr' (يوم الفطر) specifies the day, not the night. The special breaking of the fast (festival) occurs during the day.
The Hanafi proof is based on the naming convention.
3
Analyse the Shafi'i Proof
Al-Shafi'i argues that Fitr (breaking fast) happens at sunset when the fast ends, so obligation begins at sunset of the last day.
This is the root of the ikhtilaf.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi Response
The Hanafi response distinguishes between the daily breaking (at sunset) and the festival breaking (on the day of Eid). The obligation is tied to the festival, which is a daytime event.
Thus, the Hanafi position is upheld.
5
Explore Ta'jil and Ta'khir
The passage states that prepayment (ta'jil) is valid absolutely – even before Ramadan – and delay is allowed. It refutes restrictive views like al-Hasan ibn Ziyad's analogy with Udhiya.
The key reasoning: Zakat al-Fitr is a rationally understood act of devotion (ma'qul al-ma'na), so it can be given early and does not drop after the day.

Source Text

وقت صدقة الفطر
صبح يوم الفطر، فمن مات قبله أو أسلم أو ولد بعده لا تحب، وصح لو قدم أو أخر.
بر
وهو طلوع الفجر منه
قبل صبح يوم الفطر
بعد صبح يوم الفطر عليه صدقة الفطر
برطل أهل المدينة، وهو أكبر من رطل أهل بغداد؛ لأنه ثلاثون إستاراً، والرطل البغدادي عشرون إستاراً، وإذا قابلت لثمانية أرطال بالبغدادي بخمسة أرطال وثلث رطل بالمدني تجدهما سواء، فوقع الوهم لأجل ذلك، وهذا أشبه؛ لأن محمداً لم يذكر في المسألة خلاف أبي يوسف، ولو كان فيه لذكره وهو أعرف بمذهبه، ثم يعتبر نصف صاع من بر أو صاع من غيره بالوزن، فيما روى أبو يوسف عن أبي حنيفة؛ لأن الاختلاف في مقدار الصاع
سبب
كالإجماع على اعتبار الوزن، وروى محمد أنه يعتبر بالكيل؛ لأن الآثار جاءت بالصاع هو اسم للكيل. (فتح) صبح يوم الفطر: [منصوب على الظرفية، والعامل فيه "تجب"، أي تجب صدقة الفطر في صبح. (ع)] وقال الشافعي: عند غروب الشمس؛ لأن الفطر بانفصال الصوم، وذلك بالغروب من اليوم الأخير من رمضان، ولنا: أن الإضافة للاختصاص للفطر باليوم دون الليلة وذلك لأن اليوم هو المسمّى بيوم الفطر، والفرض أن يتعلق الفطر بفطر مخالف للعادة وهو اليوم لا الليل وللشافعي قولان آخران الأول بطلوع الفجر يوم العيد كمذهبنا، والثاني: بمجموع الوقتين. (عيني، مستخلص أو أسلم أحد من الكفار بعد صبح الفطر. (ع) وصح لو قدم على الوقت مطلقاً وهو الصحيح؛ لأن وجود السبب كان في صحة التعجيل؛ لأن الوجوب رأس يمونه ويلي عليه، وعند خلف بن أيوب يجوز تعجيلها بعد دخول رمضان لا قبله؛ لأنها صدقة الفطر ولا فطر قبل الشروع في الصوم، وقيل: يجوز تعجيلها في النصف الآخر من رمضان، وقيل: في العشر الأخير منه، وعند الحسن بن زياد لا يجوز تعجيلها أصلاً كالأضحية، وردّ بأن الأضحية غير معقولة فلا تكون عبادة إلا في وقت مخصوص، بخلاف التصدق، فإنه قربة معقولة المعنى، وقوله: "أو أخر" أي عن يومه وإن طالت الأداء بعده؛ لأن وقتها موسع، وعن الحسن: يسقط بمضي يوم الفطر؛ لأنها قربة اختصت بيوم العيد وتسقط بمضيه كالأضحية تسقط بمضي أيام النحر، قلنا: هي قربة معقولة المعنى، فلا تسقط بمضي الوقت كالزكاة بخلاف الأضحية. (فتح)
المدة، وصح
لو قدم: أي لو قدم صدقة الفطر على وقت الوجوب ولو قبل رمضان. (ط،ع) أو أخر: أي الصدقة عن وقت الوجوب؛ لأن وقتها موسع وهو قول العامة. (ط)
Time of Zakat al-Fitr: The morning of the day of Fitr (Eid). So whoever dies before it, or embraces Islam, or is born after it, it is not obligatory. It is valid if one gives it early or delays. The morning is the break of dawn from it. Before the morning of the day of Fitr, after the morning of the day of Fitr, upon him is Zakat al-Fitr. Al-Shafi'i said: at sunset (of the last day of Ramadan), because breaking the fast (futur) occurs with the completion of fasting, and that is at sunset. Our proof: the addition (of the word 'Fitr' to the day) indicates specificity of breaking the fast to the day, not the night; the day is called the Day of Fitr, and the obligation is connected to a breaking of the fast that is contrary to the norm, which is the day, not the night. Al-Shafi'i has two other opinions: first, at dawn of Eid day (like our school); second, at both times combined. ... It is valid to give early absolutely, and this is the correct view, because the existence of the cause (the obligation's due) does not prevent early payment. According to Khalaf ibn Ayyub, it is permissible to give early after the start of Ramadan, not before, because it is Zakat al-Fitr and there is no 'Fitr' before beginning the fast. Some say it is permissible in the second half of Ramadan, some say in the last ten days. According to al-Hasan ibn Ziyad, it is not permissible at all, like the Udhiya. This is refuted: the Udhiya is not rationally understood, so it is only an act of worship at a specific time, unlike charity, which is a rationally understood act of devotion. And his saying 'or delays' means he delays it beyond its day, even if the performance is extended afterwards, because its time is broad. According to al-Hasan, it is dropped by the passing of the day of Fitr, because it is an act of worship specific to the day of Eid and drops like the Udhiya drops with the passing of the days of Nahr. We say: it is a rationally understood act of devotion, so it does not drop with the passing of time, like Zakat, unlike the Udhiya.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage determines the time of obligation (wujub) for Zakat al-Fitr and discusses the validity of prepayment (ta'jil) and delay (ta'khir). The matn states the obligation binds at the morning (fajr) of Eid day. This is the Hanafi position. Al-Shafi'i argues it becomes obligatory at sunset of the last day of Ramadan, because 'Fitr' (breaking the fast) happens at sunset. The Hanafi response is that the 'Day of Fitr' is named as such because the day itself is the occasion for breaking the fast in a special way (festival), not the night. The passage then details various intra-Hanafi opinions on ta'jil: the correct view is that prepayment is valid at any time before Eid, even before Ramadan, because the cause (the obligation) does not prevent early payment. The least restrictive view is that it can be given after Ramadan starts; the most restrictive (al-Hasan ibn Ziyad) says not at all, analogous to Udhiya, but this is refuted because charity is rationally understood (ma'qul al-ma'na) and can be given early. Similarly, delay is allowed because the time is expansive (wasi'). Some say it drops after the day of Eid, but the Hanafi position is that it remains a debt, like Zakat, because it is a rational act of devotion. This lesson underscores the Hanafi methodology of using rational meaning (ta'lil) to extend worship times.

Key Terms
تجب (tajibu): It becomes obligatory (the time of obligation). The time of wujub is fajr of Eid day.
صدقة الفطر (sadaqat al-fitr): The obligatory charity given at the end of Ramadan, known as Zakat al-Fitr.
تعجيل (ta'jil): Giving Zakat al-Fitr before the time of obligation (wujub).
تأخير (ta'khir): Delaying the payment of Zakat al-Fitr beyond the day of Eid.
قربة معقولة (qurbah ma'qulah): An act of devotion that is rationally understood in its meaning and purpose.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is not valid because the month of Ramadan has not begun.
B) It is valid (sahih) and considered the correct view.
C) It is valid only in the last ten days of Ramadan.
D) It is not allowed because the recipient may not be needy at the time of wajub.

Key Takeaway
Zakat al-Fitr becomes wajib at fajr of Eid day, can be given early or late, and does not drop after the day; the Hanafi proof is based on the linguistic specificity of the 'Day of Fitr'.

Time of Sadaqat al-Fitr and Early/Late Payment
Ruling on the time of obligation of Sadaqat al-Fitr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the time of obligation of Sadaqat al-Fitr and explain the validity of early or late payment, citing the dalil and addressing the Shafi'i dispute.

Core Idea
Sadaqat al-Fitr becomes wajib at dawn of Eid day; early payment is valid, late payment does not drop the duty.

This lesson examines the time when Sadaqat al-Fitr becomes obligatory, based on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The Hanafi school holds that it is due at fajr of Eid day, contrary to the Shafi'i view. The passage also clarifies that paying before or after the time is valid, with the obligation remaining until paid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Sadaqat al-Fitr is wajib; its time of obligation is fajr of Eid. The matn states: 'The morning of the day of Fitr.'
The obligation is not fard because it is established by ijtihad.
2
Locate the dalil
The name 'yawm al-fitr' indicates the day is the occasion for the charity; the obligation attaches to a day contrary to habit.
3
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i places the obligation at sunset of the last day of Ramadan, arguing that breaking the fast occurs at sunset.
This is the main external dispute.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The fitr in question is the Eid day fitr, not the nightly breaking; the day is specifically designated in the name.
Also, the obligation relates to a 'breaking contrary to habit' (daytime fitr).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If a person dies between sunset of the last day of Ramadan and dawn of Eid, Hanafi says no liability, Shafi'i says liability.
Also, early payment is valid in Hanafi, while some other views restrict it.

Source Text

صبح يوم الفطر، فمن مات قبله أو أسلم أو ولد بعده لا تحب، وصح لو قدم أو أخر.

(ع)] وقال الشافعي: عند غروب الشمس؛ لأن الفطر بانفصال الصوم، وذلك بالغروب من اليوم الأخير من رمضان، ولنا: أن الإضافة للاختصاص للفطر باليوم دون الليلة وذلك لأن اليوم هو المسمّى بيوم الفطر، والفرض أن يتعلق الفطر بفطر مخالف للعادة وهو اليوم لا الليل وللشافعي قولان آخران الأول بطلوع الفجر يوم العيد كمذهبنا، والثاني: بمجموع الوقتين. (عيني، مستخلص أو أسلم أحد من الكفار بعد صبح الفطر. (ع) وصح لو قدم على الوقت مطلقاً وهو الصحيح؛ لأن وجود السبب كان في صحة التعجيل؛ لأن الوجوب رأس يمونه ويلي عليه، وعند خلف بن أيوب يجوز تعجيلها بعد دخول رمضان لا قبله؛ لأنها صدقة الفطر ولا فطر قبل الشروع في الصوم، وقيل: يجوز تعجيلها في النصف الآخر من رمضان، وقيل: في العشر الأخير منه، وعند الحسن بن زياد لا يجوز تعجيلها أصلاً كالأضحية، وردّ بأن الأضحية غير معقولة فلا تكون عبادة إلا في وقت مخصوص، بخلاف التصدق، فإنه قربة معقولة المعنى، وقوله: "أو أخر" أي عن يومه وإن طالت الأداء بعده؛ لأن وقتها موسع، وعن الحسن: يسقط بمضي يوم الفطر؛ لأنها قربة اختصت بيوم العيد وتسقط بمضيه كالأضحية تسقط بمضي أيام النحر، قلنا: هي قربة معقولة المعنى، فلا تسقط بمضي الوقت كالزكاة بخلاف الأضحية. لو قدم: أي لو قدم صدقة الفطر على وقت الوجوب ولو قبل رمضان. (ط،ع) أو أخر: أي الصدقة عن وقت الوجوب؛ لأن وقتها موسع وهو قول العامة. (ط)
Chapter of Sadaqat al-Fitr. Time of Sadaqat al-Fitr: The morning of the day of Fitr. Whoever dies before it, or becomes Muslim, or is born after it, it is not obligatory. And it is valid if he pays early or late. ... It is the dawn from it. Before the morning of Fitr, after the morning of Fitr, upon him is Sadaqat al-Fitr. The ratl of the people of Medina is larger than the ratl of Baghdad; because it is thirty ustars, and the Baghdad ratl is twenty ustars. If you compare eight Baghdad ratls with five and one-third Medina ratls, you find them equal. So confusion occurred because of this. This is more likely because Muhammad did not mention Abu Yusuf's difference in this issue; if there were one, he would have mentioned it, and he is more knowledgeable of his madhhab. Then half a sa' of wheat or a sa' of other grains is considered by weight according to Abu Yusuf's narration from Abu Hanifa, because the difference in the measure of the sa' is like consensus on considering weight. Muhammad narrated that it is by volume, because the traditions came with the sa' as a name for volume. (Fath) 'Morning of the day of Fitr' is accusative as an adverb, and the operative word is 'is obligatory', i.e., Sadaqat al-Fitr is obligatory in the morning. (Ayni) Al-Shafi'i said: At sunset, because breaking the fast is by separation from fasting, and that is at sunset of the last day of Ramadan. Our proof: The addition [al-fitr] is for specification, the breaking of the fast belongs to the day, not the night, because the day is called the day of Fitr, and the obligation is to relate the breaking to a breaking contrary to habit, which is the day, not the night. Al-Shafi'i has two other opinions: first, at dawn of the day of Eid like our madhhab; second, at both times combined. (Ayni, Mukhtasar) Or one of the disbelievers becomes Muslim after the morning of Fitr. (Ayni) And it is valid if he pays before the time absolutely, which is the correct view, because the existence of the cause permits early payment, because the obligation is a debt he bears and supervises. According to Khalaf ibn Ayyub, it is permissible to pay early after the start of Ramadan, not before, because it is the charity of breaking the fast, and there is no breaking before starting the fast. It is said: permissible to pay in the second half of Ramadan. It is said: in the last ten days. According to al-Hasan ibn Ziyad, it is not permissible to pay early at all, like the sacrificial animal. This is refuted because the sacrificial animal is not rationally understandable, so it is not an act of worship except in a specific time, unlike charity, which is a rationally understandable act of devotion. His statement 'or delayed' means after its day, even if the performance is prolonged after it, because its time is expansive. According to al-Hasan, it falls off with the passing of the day of Fitr, because it is a devotion specific to the day of Eid and falls off with its passing like the sacrificial animal falls off with the passing of the days of sacrifice. We say: It is a rationally understandable devotion, so it does not fall off with the passing of time, like zakat, unlike the sacrificial animal. (Fath) The time is expansive, and it is valid if he paid early: i.e., if he paid Sadaqat al-Fitr before the time of obligation, even before Ramadan. (T, A) Or delayed: i.e., the charity after the time of obligation, because its time is expansive, which is the common saying. (T)
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the time of obligation of Sadaqat al-Fitr. The matn states that the time is the morning of the day of Fitr (Eid al-Fitr). This is defined as the dawn of that day. The ruling covers three cases: a person who dies before that dawn, or becomes Muslim after it, or a child born after it are not liable. However, it is valid to pay early (before the time) or late (after the time). The commentary then discusses a dispute about the measurement of the sa' between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, concluding that the weight-based calculation is more correct. The time of obligation is then further discussed in a dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i, who places it at sunset of the last day of Ramadan. The Hanafi argument is that the day is specifically called 'day of Fitr', so the obligation attaches to the day, not the night. The commentary also details various opinions on early payment, with the correct view being that early payment is valid at any time because the cause (Ramadan) is established. Late payment is also valid because the time is expansive and does not drop the obligation, comparing it to zakat. The passage thus establishes the Hanafi position with proofs and addresses internal and external disputes.

Key Terms
صدقة الفطر (Sadaqat al-Fitr): The obligatory charity given at the end of Ramadan upon every free Muslim who possesses the nisab beyond his basic needs.
صاع (sa'): A measure of volume equal to approximately 2.4 kg of wheat; used for the amount of Sadaqat al-Fitr (half sa' of wheat or full sa' of dates/barley).
رطل (ratl): A unit of weight; Medinan ratl = 30 ustars (approx. 400g), Baghdad ratl = 20 ustars (approx. 260g).

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) At dawn of the day of Eid al-Fitr
C) At the moment of sighting the moon of Shawwal
D) After the Eid prayer

Key Takeaway
Sadaqat al-Fitr is wajib at dawn of Eid day; early payment is valid and late payment does not drop the obligation.

Can One Penance Cover Two Kafarat? The Hanafi Jins Distinction
Explains validity of one penance for multiple kafarat, with disputes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a single act of penance (kafarah) can fulfill only one obligation of the same jins, and identify when different jins prevent any fulfillment.

Core Idea
Same jins: one penance covers one obligation; different jins: no coverage—each requires its own act.

Zihar and other expiations require specific acts of penance. But what if someone owes two kafarat—can a single act satisfy both? The Hanafi school answers by looking at the 'jins' (type) of the cause. This lesson unpacks the rule, the internal and external disputes, and a special istihsan exception for freeing a disbelieving slave.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenarios presented
The passage presents three situations: (1) freeing two slaves for two zihar without specification, (2) freeing one slave for two zihar, (3) freeing one slave for zihar and accidental killing (qatl). Note which are valid and which are not.
The ruling hinges on whether the causes are of the same jins.
2
Define 'jins' and its legal significance
Jins refers to the category of the kafarah based on its specific requirements (e.g., zihar requires any slave; qatl requires a believing slave). Same jins means the requirements are identical; different jins means they differ.
This is the core criterion for Hanafi differentiation.
3
Trace the Hanafi position and evidence
The Hanafis argue that the Quran and Sunnah impose different conditions for different causes, proving distinct jins. For example, the verse on accidental killing (an-Nisa 4:92) explicitly requires a believing slave, whereas zihar does not. Thus, a single act cannot satisfy both.
The nass (text) for qatl is the primary evidence for requiring a believing slave.
4
Contrast with opposing views
Al-Shafi'i holds all kafarat are one jins because they share the purpose of covering sins. Zufar (within Hanafi) holds that a single act never suffices for two obligations, even if same jins. Understand each proof and the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).
The Hanafi middle ground is: valid for one if same jins, invalid for both if different jins.
5
Apply the istihsan exception
If a disbelieving slave is freed, it is valid for zihar but not for qatl (by nass). The istihsan here overrides qiyas that might otherwise require a believing slave for zihar as well. Understand why istihsan is invoked.
Istihsan is a Hanafi source of law; other schools may reject it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعن إفطار وظهار أو حرر عبدين عن ظهارين ولم يعين صح عنهما، ومثله الصيام والإطعام. وإن حرر عنهما رقبة أو صام شهرين صح عن واحد. وعن ظهار وقتل لا. أي من وجب عليه كفارتان كفارة ظهار، وكفارة قتل خطأ فأعتق رقبة مؤمنة عنهما، أو صام شهرين عنهما لم يجز عن واحد منهما. وقال الشافعي له أن يجعل عن إحداهما؛ لأن الكفارات كلها عنده جنس واحد لاتحاد المقصود، وهو الستر. والحاصل أن عند الشافعي شمول الجواز، وعند زفر شمول العدم، وعندنا: يفصل ويقال: إن اتحد الجنس كان له أن يجعل ذلك عن أيتهما شاء، وإن اختلف لا يجوز عن واحد منهما. وإنما قيدنا الرقبة بالمؤمنة؛ لأنها إن كانت كافرة جاز عن الظهار استحسانا؛ لأن الكافرة لا تصح لكفارة القتل بالنص، فتعينت للظهار.
And regarding [penance for] breaking fast and zihar: If he frees two slaves for two [acts of] zihar without specifying [which is for which], it is valid for both. The same applies to fasting and feeding. If he frees one slave for both or fasts two months [for both], it is valid for one [of them]. And for zihar and [manslaughter] killing: no. That is, if one owes two penances—a penance for zihar and a penance for accidental killing—and he frees a believing slave for both, or fasts two months for both, it is not valid for either. Al-Shafi'i said he may assign it to whichever he wishes, because in his view all penances are of one type, due to the unity of purpose, which is covering [sins]. The summary: According to al-Shafi'i, permissibility applies in both cases; according to Zufar, non-permissibility applies in both; according to us, we differentiate: if the type is the same, he may assign it to whichever he wishes; if different, it is not valid for either. We restricted [the slave] to 'believing' because if she were disbelieving, it would be valid for zihar by istihsan, since a disbelieving [slave] is not valid for the penance of killing by nass, so it is specifically assigned to zihar.
Source pages p. 490

Commentary
This passage discusses the validity of a single penance (kafarah) being applied to multiple obligations. The text distinguishes between cases where the causes (asbab) are of the same 'jins' (type) versus different. For two acts of zihar, since the penance is identical (freeing a slave, fasting two months, or feeding sixty poor), freeing two slaves without specific intention covers both. Similarly, feeding sixty poor with one sa' each for both fasting and zihar is valid because the types differ (one is for ramadan, one for zihar) but the quantity suffices. However, freeing one slave for two zihar only counts for one, as the act is a single unit insufficient for two obligations. For mixed causes like zihar and manslaughter, the penances differ in required qualities (e.g., a believing slave for qatl, any slave for zihar), so a single act cannot cover both. The Hanafi position is contrasted with al-Shafi'i (who considers all penances one type due to shared purpose) and Zufar (who rejects validity in all cases). The text also notes an istihsan ruling: if a disbelieving slave is freed, it is valid only for zihar, not qatl, since the latter requires faith by explicit text.

Key Terms
الجنس (al-jins): The type or category of the cause (sabab) that determines the specific requirements of the kafarah (e.g., zihar vs. qatl).
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): A juristic preference that overrides qiyas in certain cases; here, allowing a disbelieving slave for zihar despite general rule of needing a believer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is valid for both.
B) It is valid for one, and he may choose which.
C) It is invalid for both.
D) It is invalid unless the slave is a believer.

Key Takeaway
One act of penance can fulfill only one obligation of the same jins; if jins differ, it fulfills none.

The Obligation of Spousal Maintenance and Its Proofs
Ruling on the obligation of spousal maintenance with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on spousal maintenance, identify its four proofs, and explain the rational basis (compensation for confinement).

Core Idea
A husband must provide food, clothing, and housing for his wife—by Quran, Sunnah, consensus, and reason.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq establishes the fundamental ruling that a husband must maintain his wife. The commentator explains why the chapter is placed after divorce and provides lexical and legal definitions. We will examine the four proofs that make maintenance wajib and the underlying rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Determine what the ruling is (wajib) and to whom it applies (all wives regardless of wealth, religion, or consummation).
2
Examine the four proofs
List the Quranic verses (65:7 and 2:233), the prophetic hadith from the Farewell Sermon, the ijma, and the rational argument.
The rational argument is that maintenance compensates the wife for her confinement to the marriage.
3
Analyze the rational argument (qiyas)
Understand how the 'illa of detention (habs) extends maintenance to other cases like mudarib, executor, mufti, etc.
This shows that maintenance is not solely for wives but for anyone detained for another's benefit.
4
Understand the exception for lawful withholding
Note that maintenance remains wajib even if the wife withholds herself due to unpaid prompt mahr, as it is a lawful prevention.
This clarifies that not all refusals forfeit maintenance—only nushuz without right.

باب النفقة أي في بيان أحكامها تجب النفقة للزوجة على زوجها والكسوة بقدر حالهما ولو مانعة نفسها. باب النفقة: [وهي في اللغة ما ينفقه الإنسان على عياله. (فتح)] أورد مباحث النفقة في ذيل كتاب الطلاق؛ لأن من جملتها نفقة المطلقة، وبعضهم أوردها في ذيل كتاب النكاح لترتب نفقة المنكوحة، وبعضهم في كتاب على حدة لما فيها من نفقة ذوي الأرحام والمماليك وهي في اللغة: ما ينفقه الإنسان على عياله، وفي الشرع: الطعام والكسوة والسكنى. قيل: هي مشتقة النفوق بمعنى الهلاك أو النفاق بمعنى الرواج؛ لأن بها هلاك المال أو لأنها تروج في مصالح الحال، ونفقة الغير على الغير تجب بثلاثة أشياء: بالزوجية وبالقرابة وبالملك، وكذا تحب بسبب حبس النفس لمصالح الغير كالمضارب والوصي، أو لمصالح العامة كالمفتي والقاضي والوالي والعامل في الصدقات والمقاتلة. (ط) والكسوة أي تجب الكسوة لها عليه أيضاً. (ع) بقدر حالهما: [ أي حال الزوجين في اليسار والإعسار. (ط، ع] أي تجب النفقة والكسوة لها عليه بقدر حالهما في اليسار والإعسار ، فإن كان الزوجان موسرين كان لها نفقة اليسار، وإن كانا معسرين كان لها نفقة الإعسار وإن كانت معسرة والزوج موسر فنفقتها ما دون نفقة الموسرات فوق نفقة المعسرات، وهذا اختيار المصنف، وعليه الفتوى، وقال الكرخي والشافعي: يعتبر حال الزوج؛ لقوله تعالى: وَلِيُنْفِقْ ذُو سَعَةٍ مِنْ سَعَتِهِ ولنا: قوله عليها لهند امرأة أبي سفيان: خذي من مال زوجك ما يكفيك وولدك بالمعروف" اعتبر حالها. والفقيرة لا تفتقر إلى كفاية الموسرات، فلا معنى للزيادة، وأما النص فنحن نقول بموجبه : أنه مخاطب بقدر وسعه، والباقي دين في ذمته ومعنى قوله: "بالمعروف الوسط، وهو الواجب، واعتبر حالهما معاً جمعاً بين الآية والحديث؛ لأن الآية تقتضي اعتبار حاله والحديث يقتضي اعتبار حالها فاعتبرنا حالهما عملاً بهما. (فتح، مص) ولو مانعة إلخ: [واصل بما قبلها أي ولو كانت المرأة مانعة من التسليم تجب النفقة. (ع)] متصل بما قبله أي تحب النفقة لها وإن امتعنت من تسليم نفسها لأجل قبض المهر الذي تعورف تقديمه في البلاد والزمان؛ لأنه منع بحق
Chapter of Maintenance: i.e., explaining its rulings. Maintenance is obligatory for the wife upon her husband, and clothing, according to the condition of both, even if she withholds herself. Chapter of Maintenance: [Linguistically, it is what a man spends on his dependents. (Fath)] He placed the discussions of maintenance at the end of the Book of Divorce because among them is the maintenance of the divorced woman, and some placed them at the end of the Book of Marriage due to the connection to maintenance of the married woman, and some placed them in a separate chapter because it includes maintenance of relatives and slaves. In language: what a man spends on his dependents. In law: food, clothing, and lodging. It is said it is derived from nufuq (perishing) or nifaq (circulation) because through it wealth perishes or because it circulates for the interests of the situation. The maintenance of another upon another is obligatory by three things: marriage, kinship, and ownership. It is also obligatory due to detaining oneself for the interests of others, like the mudarib and executor, or for public interests like the mufti, judge, governor, zakat collector, and fighter. (Fath) For the wife: [absolutely, whether she is taken to the husband's abode or not, whether she is Muslim or disbeliever, rich or poor, consummated or not. (Miskin)] By the Book, Sunnah, consensus, and a rational proof. As for the Book: His saying, 'Let the wealthy spend according to his wealth' (65:7), and His saying, 'And upon the father is their provision and clothing according to what is reasonable' (2:233). As for the Sunnah: It is narrated that he said in the Farewell Sermon: 'Fear Allah concerning women... and they have the right upon you of their provision and clothing in a reasonable manner.' As for consensus: The ummah has agreed that maintenance and lodging are obligatory for the wife upon her husband. As for the rational: Because maintenance is due as a recompense for confinement. This applies when the marriage is valid, whether the husband is rich or poor, present or absent. (Tabyin al-Haqa'iq) And clothing: i.e., clothing is also obligatory for her upon him. According to the condition of both: i.e., the condition of both spouses regarding affluence and straitened circumstances. So maintenance and clothing are obligatory for her upon him according to the condition of both in affluence and straitened circumstances. If both spouses are wealthy, she gets the maintenance of the wealthy; if both are poor, she gets the maintenance of the poor. If she is poor and the husband is wealthy, her maintenance is less than that of wealthy women and above that of poor women. This is the author's choice, and upon it is the fatwa. Al-Karakhi and al-Shafi'i said: Only the husband's condition is considered, due to His saying, 'Let the wealthy spend according to his wealth.' Our proof: His saying to Hind, the wife of Abu Sufyan: 'Take from your husband's wealth what suffices you and your child in a reasonable manner,' which considered her condition. The poor woman does not need the sufficiency of wealthy women, so there is no meaning to increase. As for the text, we apply it according to its import: he is addressed according to his capacity, and the remainder is a debt on his liability. The meaning of His saying 'in a reasonable manner' is the middle, which is obligatory, and the condition of both is considered together to combine the verse and the hadith. Because the verse requires considering his condition, and the hadith requires considering her condition, so we considered both to act on both. (Fath, Misbah) And even if she withholds herself: [Connected to what preceded: i.e., even if the woman withholds herself from submission, maintenance is obligatory. ('Ayni)] Connected to what preceded: maintenance is obligatory for her even if she refrains from surrendering herself in order to receive the mahr that is customarily advanced in the country and time, because it is a lawful prevention.
Source pages p. 523

Commentary
This passage begins the chapter on maintenance (nafaqah) from Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The commentator first explains why the author placed this chapter at the end of the Book of Divorce rather than after marriage: because it covers maintenance for divorced women as well. He provides lexical and legal definitions: linguistically it is spending on dependents; legally it includes food, clothing, and lodging. The obligation arises from three causes: marriage, kinship, and ownership. It also applies to those detained for public service (e.g., mufti, judge, soldier). The core ruling is that a husband must provide maintenance and clothing to his wife. Four proofs are given: Quran (65:7 and 2:233), Sunnah (the Prophet's command in the Farewell Sermon), consensus, and rational argument (maintenance is compensation for the wife's confinement). This obligation applies to all wives—Muslim or not, rich or poor, consummated or not, present or absent husband. The amount of maintenance is determined by the financial status of both spouses (the author's choice, and the fatwa position). If both are wealthy, she gets rich maintenance; if both are poor, poor maintenance; if she is poor and he is wealthy, she gets an intermediate amount. This differs from al-Karakhi and al-Shafi'i, who consider only the husband's status. The Hanafi proof includes the hadith of Hind, where the Prophet told her to take what suffices, considering her need. The verse 'Let the wealthy spend according to his wealth' is interpreted as the husband's capacity, with any shortfall becoming a debt. The phrase 'in a reasonable manner' is interpreted as the middle standard, which is obligatory. The ruling that both statuses are considered is a reconciliation of the proofs. Finally, the text affirms that maintenance is due even if the wife withholds herself from her husband because she has not received her prompt mahr (a customary practice), as that prevention is lawful and does not forfeit her right to support.

Key Terms
النفقة (al-nafaqah): In legal terminology, it refers to food, clothing, and lodging that are obligatory for a husband to provide for his wife, and by extension for relatives and slaves.
الكسوة (al-kiswah): Clothing that the husband must provide for his wife as part of maintenance.
المعروف (al-ma'rūf): A reasonable and customary standard, interpreted as the middle level between extravagance and stinginess, taking into account the financial states of both spouses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the rational basis (al-ma'qul) for making spousal maintenance wajib?
A) The husband's love for his wife
B) Compensation for the wife's confinement (احتباس)
C) The wife's financial need regardless of marriage
D) The husband's ability to pay

Key Takeaway
Maintenance for the wife is wajib by multiple proofs and is compensation for her confinement in the marriage.

Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate
10 min
Determining the Amount of Maintenance: Considering Both Spouses
Dispute on the criteria for determining maintenance amount

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to compare the Hanafi position on determining maintenance amount (considering both spouses) with the view of al-Karakhi and al-Shafi'i, and explain the Hanafi evidence from the hadith of Hind.

Core Idea
Maintenance amount is based on both spouses' financial status, combining Quran and Sunnah.

This passage presents the Hanafi position on how much maintenance a wife should receive. The author chooses to consider the condition of both spouses, contradicting al-Karakhi and al-Shafi'i who consider only the husband's wealth. We will examine the proofs on both sides and see how the Hanafi school reconciles the texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed point
What is the dispute? It is about whose financial status determines the amount of maintenance: only the husband's, or both spouses'.
2
State the Hanafi position
The author chooses that both spouses' conditions (يسار وإعسار) are considered. If both are wealthy, rich maintenance; both poor, poor maintenance; if mixed, intermediate.
This is the mufta bihi position.
3
Present the opposing view
Al-Karakhi and al-Shafi'i say only the husband's condition matters, citing Quran 65:7 'Let the wealthy spend according to his wealth'.
4
Analyze the Hanafi proof from the hadith of Hind
The Prophet told Hind to take from her husband's wealth 'what suffices you and your child in a reasonable manner,' considering her needs. This shows the wife's condition matters.
The Hanafis argue that the verse addresses the husband's capacity, and any shortfall is a debt on him.
5
Understand the reconciliation
Both proofs (verse and hadith) are combined: the verse indicates the husband's capacity, the hadith indicates the wife's need, so both are considered to act on both texts.
This is a classic example of applying the principle of working with all dalils when possible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب النفقة أي في بيان أحكامها تجب النفقة للزوجة على زوجها والكسوة بقدر حالهما ولو مانعة نفسها. باب النفقة: [وهي في اللغة ما ينفقه الإنسان على عياله. (فتح)] أورد مباحث النفقة في ذيل كتاب الطلاق؛ لأن من جملتها نفقة المطلقة، وبعضهم أوردها في ذيل كتاب النكاح لترتب نفقة المنكوحة، وبعضهم في كتاب على حدة لما فيها من نفقة ذوي الأرحام والمماليك وهي في اللغة: ما ينفقه الإنسان على عياله، وفي الشرع: الطعام والكسوة والسكنى. قيل: هي مشتقة النفوق بمعنى الهلاك أو النفاق بمعنى الرواج؛ لأن بها هلاك المال أو لأنها تروج في مصالح الحال، ونفقة الغير على الغير تجب بثلاثة أشياء: بالزوجية وبالقرابة وبالملك، وكذا تحب بسبب حبس النفس لمصالح الغير كالمضارب والوصي، أو لمصالح العامة كالمفتي والقاضي والوالي والعامل في الصدقات والمقاتلة. (فتح) للزوجة: [مطلقاً سواء كانت تزف إلى مبيت زوجها أو لم تزف، وسواء كانت مسلمة أو كافرة، غنية أو فقيرة مدخولاً بها أو لا. (مسكين)] بالكتاب والسنة والإجماع وضرب من المعقول، أما الكتاب: فقوله تعالى : اليُنْفِقْ ذُو سَعَةٍ مِنْ سَعَتِه الله (الطلاق:۷)، وقوله تعالى: وَعَلَى الْمَوْلُودِ لَهُ رِزْقُهُنَّ وَكِسْوَتُهُنَّ بِالْمَعْرُوفِ ﴾ (البقرة:٢٣٣)، وأما السنة: روي أنه عليها قال في خطبة الوداع: "اتقوا الله في "النساء" إلى أن قال: "ولهن عليكم رزقهن وكسوتهن بالمعروف"، وأما الإجماع: فإن الأمة أجمعت على أن النفقة والسكنى واجبتان للزوجة على زوجها، وأما المعقول: فلأن النفقة تجب جزاء الاحتباس، وهذا إذا كان النكاح صحيحا [تبيين الحقائق: ٣٠١/٣] على زوجها غنيا أو فقيرا حاضرا أو غائباً . (ط) والكسوة أي تجب الكسوة لها عليه أيضاً. (ع) بقدر حالهما: [ أي حال الزوجين في اليسار والإعسار. (ط، ع] أي تجب النفقة والكسوة لها عليه بقدر حالهما في اليسار والإعسار ، فإن كان الزوجان موسرين كان لها نفقة اليسار، وإن كانا معسرين كان لها نفقة الإعسار وإن كانت معسرة والزوج موسر فنفقتها ما دون نفقة الموسرات فوق نفقة المعسرات، وهذا اختيار المصنف، وعليه الفتوى، وقال الكرخي والشافعي: يعتبر حال الزوج؛ لقوله تعالى: وَلِيُنْفِقْ ذُو سَعَةٍ مِنْ سَعَتِهِ ولنا: قوله عليها لهند امرأة أبي سفيان: خذي من مال زوجك ما يكفيك وولدك بالمعروف" اعتبر حالها. والفقيرة لا تفتقر إلى كفاية الموسرات، فلا معنى للزيادة، وأما النص فنحن نقول بموجبه : أنه مخاطب بقدر وسعه، والباقي دين في ذمته ومعنى قوله: "بالمعروف الوسط، وهو الواجب، واعتبر حالهما معاً جمعاً بين الآية والحديث؛ لأن الآية تقتضي اعتبار حاله والحديث يقتضي اعتبار حالها فاعتبرنا حالهما عملاً بهما.
